# C#-Style Value-Type SemIR

This contract records the first typed value-place layer used to move `struct` toward C# value-type semantics and IL2CPP-style lowering.

## Scope

`struct` locals that have `ZR_FUNCTION_FRAME_SLOT_KIND_INLINE_STRUCT` frame layout are treated as inline value payloads for SemIR metadata. The interpreter still executes the existing bytecode path, but SemIR now preserves the value-type intent so AOT lowering does not have to infer it from untyped stack mutations.

The initial opcode family is:

- `VALUE_ADDR`: address/place for a frame value slot.
- `FIELD_ADDR`: address/place for a field inside an inline struct receiver.
- `LOAD_VALUE`: typed load from a value place into a destination slot.
- `STORE_VALUE`: typed store into a value place.
- `INIT_VALUE`: reserved for layout-aware zero/default construction.
- `COPY_VALUE`: layout-aware by-value copy between inline struct slots.
- `CALL_TYPED`: typed call metadata for known call sites whose return destination has proven inline struct layout.
- `RETURN_TYPED`: typed return metadata for single-result inline struct return sources.

## Current Lowering

`compiler_semir.c` maps known inline struct bytecode patterns into metadata rows:

- `GET_MEMBER_SLOT` on an inline struct receiver emits `FIELD_ADDR` followed by `LOAD_VALUE`.
- `SET_MEMBER_SLOT` on an inline struct receiver emits `FIELD_ADDR` followed by `STORE_VALUE`.
- `SET_STACK` between inline struct slots emits `COPY_VALUE`; if the source was staged through the immediately preceding `GET_STACK`, the original inline struct source slot is recorded.
- `FUNCTION_CALL` / `KNOWN_VM_CALL` with a result slot that has proven inline struct layout emits `CALL_TYPED`. The destination slot is the return payload slot, `operand0` is the callee slot, and `operand1` is the bytecode argument count.
- Single-result `FUNCTION_RETURN` from a proven inline struct source emits `RETURN_TYPED`. The destination slot and `operand0` both identify the source return payload slot.

`FIELD_ADDR.operand0` is the receiver slot. `FIELD_ADDR.operand1`, `LOAD_VALUE.operand1`, and `STORE_VALUE.operand1` carry the member/cache index used by the source bytecode. `COPY_VALUE.operand0` is the source inline struct slot. Call-result temporaries can recover `typeTableIndex` through matching inline `typeLayoutId` frame-slot layout when there is no direct typed-local binding for the temporary slot.

## AOT Boundary

The AOT ExecIR name table recognizes the new opcodes. These value-place opcodes currently add no runtime contract bits because they are intended to lower into direct frame/field/copy expressions once AotExecIR consumes layout metadata.

The archived AotExecIR frame layout now mirrors inline frame byte metadata:

- `SZrAotExecIrFrameLayout.frameByteSize`
- `SZrAotExecIrFrameLayout.frameByteAlign`
- `SZrAotExecIrFrameLayout.slotLayoutCount`
- `SZrAotExecIrFrameLayout.slotLayouts`

Each `SZrAotExecIrFrameSlotLayout` copies stack slot, byte offset, byte size, byte align, type layout id, slot kind, and parameter marker from `SZrFunctionFrameSlotLayout`. This gives future generated C lowering a direct route from `FIELD_ADDR` / `LOAD_VALUE` / `STORE_VALUE` / `COPY_VALUE` to frame byte spans without reverse-engineering layout from flat stack counts.

The archived `aot_c` writer now has a first value-place lowering surface in `backend_aot_c_value_semir.*` plus the focused field module `backend_aot_c_value_semir_fields.*`. `backend_aot_write_c_value_semir_for_function()` receives `SZrState`, walks each function's AotExecIR SemIR rows, finds frame-slot byte layout with `backend_aot_c_find_frame_slot_layout()`, and dispatches field address/load/store rows to the field module. The field module resolves struct field metadata with `ZrCore_Function_ResolvePrototypeFrameFieldLayout()` and emits value-place lowering annotations for:

- `FIELD_ADDR` -> `zr_aot_value_field_addr`
- `LOAD_VALUE` -> `zr_aot_value_load`
- `STORE_VALUE` -> `zr_aot_value_store`
- `COPY_VALUE` -> `zr_aot_value_copy`
- `CALL_TYPED` -> `zr_aot_value_call_typed`
- `RETURN_TYPED` -> `zr_aot_value_return_typed`

For equal-sized copy spans it records the current generated-frame ABI shape: `memmove((TZrByte *)frame.slotBase + dstOffset, (const TZrByte *)frame.slotBase + srcOffset, size)`. Field address, field load, and field store annotations now record `base byte offset + field byte offset` expressions after resolving the member/cache index to `SZrFunctionFrameFieldLayout`. Typed call/return annotations record the involved frame layout and type id, and the first POD executable path now consumes the same layout facts.

`backend_aot_c_value_semir.c` is now the value-SemIR orchestrator and copy/call/return lowering surface. Field-specific helpers, including primitive field transfer, embedded `SZrTypeValue` transfer, layout-aware nested inline struct transfer, and the explicit unsupported resolved-field boundary, live in `backend_aot_c_value_semir_fields.c`. This keeps the value-place field responsibility below the large-file threshold and gives future field policies a narrow module boundary instead of growing the orchestrator.

The first executable M5 steps are now inline `COPY_VALUE` lowering and primitive POD field load/store lowering. `backend_aot_try_write_c_value_semir_for_exec_instruction()` checks the current exec instruction for a matching value SemIR row:

- `COPY_VALUE` on matching inline struct `SET_STACK` / `GET_STACK` sites now emits a generated type-layout gate and skips the old generic stack-copy helper. The generated C resolves `ZrCore_Function_ResolvePrototypeFrameTypeLayout(frame.function, typeLayoutId, state)`, uses `ZrCore_TypeLayout_CanRawCopy()` to keep POD struct copies on `memmove`, and uses `ZrCore_TypeLayout_CopyInline()` for non-POD field-aware copies such as structs with embedded `SZrTypeValue` fields.
- `LOAD_VALUE` on matching inline struct `GET_MEMBER_SLOT` sites resolves the field layout, reads the primitive field bytes from `(const TZrByte *)frame.slotBase + baseOffset + fieldOffset`, writes the scalar result into the byte-backed destination `SZrTypeValue`, and mirrors that result into the dense `frame.slotBase + destinationSlot` view. Generated code may still have direct typed arithmetic, branch, or return paths that read the dense view while the byte-frame ABI migration is incomplete, so field loads must keep both views coherent.
- `STORE_VALUE` on matching inline struct `SET_MEMBER_SLOT` sites resolves the field layout, prefers a populated dense `frame.slotBase + sourceSlot` source over the byte-backed source view, converts the scalar `SZrTypeValue` to the field primitive type, and copies the primitive bytes into `(TZrByte *)frame.slotBase + baseOffset + fieldOffset`. This prevents stale byte-backed scratch values from overriding newer direct arithmetic results written to the dense slot.
- `LOAD_VALUE` / `STORE_VALUE` on matching inline struct fields that are stored as embedded `SZrTypeValue` cells now emit `zr_aot_value_exec_field_value_slot_load` / `zr_aot_value_exec_field_value_slot_store` and use `ZrCore_Value_Copy` directly between the frame byte field and the scalar destination/source slot. Value-slot loads also mirror the copied field into the dense destination, and value-slot stores prefer the dense source when it is materialized. This is the first AOT managed/reference field access slice; copy/drop ownership for whole non-POD structs still belongs to later layout-aware copy/drop lowering.
- `LOAD_VALUE` / `STORE_VALUE` on matching nested inline struct fields now emit `zr_aot_value_exec_field_inline_struct_load` / `zr_aot_value_exec_field_inline_struct_store` when the field `typeLayoutId` and byte size match the inline destination/source slot. The generated C resolves the field `SZrTypeLayout` with `ZrCore_Function_ResolvePrototypeFrameTypeLayout(frame.function, typeLayoutId, state)`, checks the emitted field byte size, keeps POD field layouts on overlap-safe `memmove`, and routes non-POD field layouts through `ZrCore_TypeLayout_CopyInline(state, ...)`. This mirrors whole-struct `COPY_VALUE` semantics for nested value fields instead of unconditionally raw-copying embedded ownership/value payloads.
- When `LOAD_VALUE` / `STORE_VALUE` resolves an inline struct field but the field is still outside the executable subset, for example a mismatched nested inline struct transfer, the generated C emits `zr_aot_value_unsupported_field_load` / `zr_aot_value_unsupported_field_store`, calls `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state, "unsupported AOT value SemIR field ...")`, and exits through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()`. Unresolved or dynamic field access still falls through to the declared runtime member contract; proven value-type fields do not silently fall back to `GetMemberSlot` / `SetMemberSlot`.
- `CALL_TYPED` on matching static/direct POD struct return sites resolves the caller destination type layout with `ZrCore_Function_ResolvePrototypeFrameTypeLayout`, checks the generated-frame destination byte size, stages the callable and arguments at `ZrCore_Function_GetCallInfoFrameStorageTop(state, frame.callInfo)`, resolves callable metadata from the callee slot with `ZrCore_Closure_GetMetadataFunctionFromValue`, prepares the resolved VM call with `ZrCore_Function_PreCallPreparedResolvedVmFunctionWithArgumentSource`, invokes the generated callee thunk, posts through `ZrCore_Function_PostCall`, and refreshes the active caller frame. Passing the caller `frame.slotBase` and source argument start lets the core runtime copy byte-backed VALUE parameters from the original generated frame while still using the staged call window for VM call setup.
- `RETURN_TYPED` on matching single inline struct return sites resolves the callee source type layout with `ZrCore_Function_ResolvePrototypeFrameTypeLayout`, checks the inline source byte size, publishes the source slot as `state->stackTop`, and lets core post-call route the payload through `ZrCore_Function_TryCopyInlineFrameReturnValue`.

Generated AOT C functions now also have a first value-frame cleanup boundary. The generated guard macro uses `ZR_AOT_C_RETURN(expr)` instead of emitting direct `return` statements from normal return, tail return, unsupported-dispatch, and failure paths. Each generated function records `zr_aot_frame_started`, a `zr_aot_return_value`, and `zr_aot_skip_drop_slot`, then exits through `zr_aot_function_exit`. `backend_aot_c_frame_cleanup.*` emits reverse frame-layout cleanup for inline struct slots: it resolves each slot's `SZrTypeLayout` from `frame.function`, skips the typed inline return source slot when that source must remain available for core post-call return movement, and calls `ZrCore_TypeLayout_DropInline` only when the resolved layout has a non-`NONE` drop kind. This does not complete hidden-return ownership or exception-aware partial initialization; it prevents the generated C path from bypassing the existing layout-driven drop contract once non-POD inline value slots are active.

Generated AOT C failure exits now report directly from the generated guard macro. `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` calls `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state, "generated AOT function failed: functionIndex=%u instructionIndex=%u", ...)` with deterministic function metadata and then exits through `ZR_AOT_C_RETURN(0)`. Generated functions that still need a frame descriptor declare `ZrAotGeneratedFrame frame = {0};`; descriptor-free pure scalar functions instead rely on the function-local `zr_aot_function_index` path. The checked C backend no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_FailGeneratedFunction(state, &frame)`; the remaining generated-C runtime boundary in `backend_aot_c*.c` is the private loaded-module context lookup.

Generated AOT C frame setup now owns simple setup diagnostics and the loaded-module context boundary directly when a generated function still needs stack frame setup or a frame descriptor. That full setup path calls `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ResolveGeneratedModuleContext(state, functionIndex, &zr_aot_context)` because loaded AOT records, function tables, generated thunk tables, module publication state, and cached frame slot counts are private runtime-loader metadata, not instruction execution behavior. The public context type is named `ZrAotGeneratedModuleContext` to keep that boundary explicit. After that boundary, generated C validates the active call frame, reports `generated AOT function has no call frame` through `ZrCore_Debug_RunError`, initializes frame slot spans directly, and populates only the frame fields that remaining legacy C paths still read when `includeFrameDescriptor` is true. Export-context fields are additionally gated by `includeExportContext`, which currently comes from the generated function's `publishExports` predicate. Descriptor-free zero-byte pure scalar functions now take an empty entry setup path: frame setup returns before emitting any generated-C setup block, and the first focused body block after the function metadata locals is `zr_aot_scalar_locals_begin`. Runtime execution-mode reporting is preserved by the private `aot_runtime_mark_record_executed()` helper at the AOT record-entry boundary, with the full context and shim paths reusing the same helper. The focused i64 native-to-VM return packaging is now isolated in `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReturnI64(state, value)`: generated C passes the scalar local to that boundary helper and no longer declares `SZrCallInfo`, constructs a caller `SZrTypeValue *`, closes closures, copies constructor receivers back, releases prior ownership payloads, or writes return-slot fields inline. That helper now lives in `zr_vm_library/src/zr_vm_library/aot_runtime/aot_runtime_return.c`; the private `aot_runtime_internal.h` exposes only the opaque runtime-state type, runtime-state lookup, and failure reporting needed by boundary modules. Setup no longer emits `frame.recordHandle`, `frame.functionIndex`, instruction observation fields, observation policy initialization, default debug-hook line overrides, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetGeneratedContext()`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetObservationPolicy()`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_DefaultObservationMask()`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_BeginGeneratedFunction()`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_MarkGeneratedFunctionExecuted()`, or `zr_aot_generated_frame_setup` for descriptor-free zero-byte pure scalar bodies. `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetObservationPolicy()` and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_DefaultObservationMask()` remain available for tests and non-generated policy queries.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 typed-return route split moves scalar native-to-VM typed return route selection out of the aggregate function-body dispatcher. `backend_aot_c_typed_return.{h,c}` now owns the i64/bool/u64/f64 scalar-local return predicates and typed return writer calls; `FUNCTION_RETURN` in `backend_aot_c_function_body.c` delegates to `backend_aot_try_write_c_typed_return(...)` before falling back to the generic value-SemIR and ordinary direct-return paths. This is route ownership support work only: it preserves the existing return helper semantics while keeping broader full typed ABI, inline struct returns, `in`/`out` writeback, deopt/dynamic bridges, and dynamic value access hardening open for later 07-S5 slices.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 expression direct-return scalarization extends the scalar-local return proof from explicit typed locals to direct bool/u64/f64 expression result slots. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals.c` now records destination coverage for typed expression result opcodes through `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_kind_from_result_opcode(...)` and `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_record_result_destinations(...)`; the return-boundary liveness scan and constant skip proof use the shared kind-based `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_can_return_kind_local(..., expectedKind, ZR_FALSE)` predicate instead of the previous i64-only return stop. Generated C for `return left > right;`, `return left + right;` over `uint`, and `return left + right;` over `float` now emits bool/u64/f64 MethodInfo return signatures and typed native-to-VM return helpers directly from `zr_aot_bN` / `zr_aot_uN` / `zr_aot_fN`, with no generic frame-slot return and no expression-result `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination` materialization. This closes the direct-expression subset only; full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and broader 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 f64 comparison expression-return scalarization closes the remaining `float` comparison -> `bool` direct-return gap inside the same expression-return subset. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals.c` now treats `LOGICAL_*_FLOAT` opcodes as bool result writes while recognizing their left/right operands as f64 scalar-local reads; `backend_aot_c_scalar_semir.c` now has a scalar f64 compare writer parallel to the existing i64/u64 compare routes. Generated C for `return left > right;` over `float` emits `zr_aot_scalar_exec_f64_compare`, writes `zr_aot_bN = (TZrBool)(zr_aot_fL op zr_aot_fR)`, publishes a bool MethodInfo return signature, and returns via `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReturnBool`; it no longer uses `zr_aot_compare_exec_float`, generic frame-slot return, or expression-result `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination`. This remains a narrow 07-S5 slice; full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 f64 unary expression-return scalarization covers `return -value;` over `float`. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals.c` now classifies `NEG_FLOAT` as an f64 result opcode and f64 scalar-local consumer; `backend_aot_write_c_direct_neg_float(...)` receives the exec instruction index so it can prove the source f64 local is written and the destination value slot can be skipped. Generated C for the new `f64_neg_expr` fixture emits `zr_aot_scalar_exec_f64_unary`, writes `zr_aot_fN = -zr_aot_fM`, publishes an f64 MethodInfo return signature, and returns via `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReturnF64`; it no longer uses `zr_aot_arith_exec_float_unary`, generic frame-slot return, or expression-result `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination`. Full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 i64 unary expression-return scalarization covers `return -value;` over signed integers. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals.c` now classifies `NEG_SIGNED` as an i64 result opcode and signed i64 local consumer, and `backend_aot_write_c_direct_neg_signed(...)` receives the exec instruction index so it can prove the source i64 local is written and the destination value slot can be skipped. Generated C for the new `i64_neg_expr` fixture emits `zr_aot_scalar_constant_i64_local`, `zr_aot_scalar_exec_i64_unary`, writes `zr_aot_sN = -zr_aot_sM`, publishes an i64 MethodInfo return signature, and returns via `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReturnI64`; it no longer uses `zr_aot_value_exec_primitive_constant`, `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination`, or `zr_aot_arith_exec_signed_unary` for this direct-return chain. Full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 i64 bit-not expression-return coverage locks `return ~value;` over signed integers. The new `i64_bit_not_expr` generated-product fixture shows the existing `BITWISE_NOT` scalar-local/result-local proof already emits `zr_aot_scalar_exec_i64_bit_not`, keeps the result in `zr_aot_sN`, publishes an i64 MethodInfo return signature, and returns via `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReturnI64`; it does not use `zr_aot_bitwise_exec_unary`, expression-result `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination`, or `zr_aot_value_exec_primitive_constant`. No production code change was required for this coverage slice. Full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 i64 binary bitwise expression-return coverage locks `return left & right;` over signed integers. The new `i64_bitwise_and_expr` generated-product fixture shows the existing binary bitwise scalar-local/result-local proof already emits `zr_aot_scalar_exec_i64_bitwise`, keeps the result in `zr_aot_sN`, publishes an i64 MethodInfo return signature, and returns via `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReturnI64`; it does not use `zr_aot_bitwise_exec_binary`, expression-result `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination`, or `zr_aot_value_exec_primitive_constant`. No production code change was required for this coverage slice. Full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 i64 two-arg state-free typed direct-call ABI narrows pure signed integer two-parameter thunks from `static TZrInt64 fn(struct SZrState *state, TZrInt64, TZrInt64)` to `static TZrInt64 fn(TZrInt64, TZrInt64)` for add/subtract/multiply and bitwise AND/OR/XOR. `backend_aot_c_can_emit_typed_i64_two_arg_state_free_thunk()` separates those no-runtime-error shapes from divide/modulo, `backend_aot_can_write_c_static_direct_i64_two_arg_call()` returns whether the call writer must pass `state`, and `backend_aot_write_c_static_direct_i64_two_arg_function_call()` emits either the state-free call or the existing stateful call. Generated multiply and bitwise-OR fixtures now show no `state` in the thunk signature or direct call, while generated divide keeps `state` for `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state, ...)`. This is still a narrow signed-i64 two-arg ABI slice; no/one/three-arg state-free decisions, u64/f64/bool ABI parity, full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 i64 no/one-arg state-free typed direct-call ABI applies the same state removal to signed integer thunks that never need runtime state. No-arg constant-return thunks now emit `static TZrInt64 zr_aot_typed_i64_fn_N(void)` and are called as `zr_aot_typed_i64_fn_N()`. One-arg identity, negate, bit-not, constant bitwise, and constant arithmetic thunks now emit `static TZrInt64 zr_aot_typed_i64_fn_N(TZrInt64 zr_aot_arg0)` and are called with the scalar local only. The generated divide fixture remains stateful through the two-arg path, preserving runtime error reporting. This leaves the i64 three-arg state-free decision and cross-type ABI parity for later 07-S5 slices.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 i64 three-arg state-free typed direct-call ABI completes the signed integer arity sweep for pure direct-call thunks. Add/subtract/multiply and bitwise AND/OR/XOR three-parameter thunks now emit `static TZrInt64 zr_aot_typed_i64_fn_N(TZrInt64 zr_aot_arg0, TZrInt64 zr_aot_arg1, TZrInt64 zr_aot_arg2)` and are called as `zr_aot_typed_i64_fn_N(zr_aot_sA, zr_aot_sB, zr_aot_sC)`. Three-arg divide/modulo remain stateful so their generated zero-denominator guards can call `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state, ...)`. This closes only the signed i64 state-free direct-call ABI slice; u64/f64/bool parity, full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 u64 two/three-arg state-free typed direct-call ABI completes the current unsigned scalar direct-call state-removal pass for pure multi-arg thunks. Two-arg and three-arg u64 add/subtract/multiply plus bitwise AND/OR/XOR thunks now emit state-free `TZrUInt64` signatures and call sites pass only u64 scalar locals. Unsigned divide/modulo keep `struct SZrState *state` because their generated zero-denominator paths still call `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state, ...)`. The u64 route proof now returns `outPassStateToThunk`, and the call writer chooses the stateful or state-free call text. Focused validation passed typed-call contracts 4/0, u64 shared-library smoke 25/0, and source contracts 19/0; generated C grep confirmed add cases are state-free while divide cases remain stateful. This leaves f64/bool ABI parity, full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, performance/SZrValue counters, and stages 08-12 open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 f64 state-free typed direct-call ABI removes runtime state from floating-point direct-call thunks that do not need error reporting. No-arg f64 constant-return and one-arg f64 identity/negate/nonzero constant arithmetic/modulo thunks now emit state-free `TZrFloat64` signatures and calls. Pure f64 two-arg and three-arg add/subtract/multiply thunks also emit state-free signatures and call sites pass only f64 scalar locals. F64 divide/modulo with dynamic denominators keep `struct SZrState *state` so generated zero-denominator paths can call `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state, ...)`. Focused validation passed typed-call contracts 4/0, f64 shared-library smoke 19/0, and source contracts 19/0; generated C grep confirmed add cases are state-free while divide cases remain stateful. This leaves bool ABI parity, full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, performance/SZrValue counters, and stages 08-12 open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 bool state-free typed direct-call ABI removes runtime state from bool-return direct-call thunks that do not need error reporting. No-arg bool constant-return, one-arg bool identity/logical-not, bool two-arg equality/logical, and bool three-arg logical thunks now emit state-free `TZrBool` signatures and calls. I64, u64, and f64 two-arg comparison thunks returning bool also emit state-free signatures, with call sites passing only the corresponding scalar locals. Focused validation passed typed-call contracts 4/0, bool shared-library smoke 28/0, and source contracts 19/0; generated C grep confirmed bool no/two/three-arg and mixed comparison bool calls no longer pass `state`. This leaves full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, performance/SZrValue counters, and stages 08-12 open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 scalar typed direct-call aggregate guardrail adds generated-product coverage for the current i64/u64/f64/bool state-free scalar direct-call ABI. The guardrail compiles a mixed scalar fixture, emits AOT C, and requires all four typed thunk families to expose state-free two-arg signatures and direct-call markers while rejecting typed-destination materialization, stack-sync markers, runtime call fallback, and `state` as the first thunk argument. It also scopes into each generated scalar typed-thunk body and rejects interpreter environment symbols plus `SZrTypeValue`, confirming the bodies are direct C returns. Validation first failed because the guardrail target still only exposed core dependencies; after linking parser/core/library support, `zr_vm_aot_c_guardrail_contracts_test` passed 6/0 and generated C grep confirmed all four direct calls pass only scalar locals. This is an aggregate guardrail, not 07-S5 closure; full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, performance/SZrValue counters, and stages 08-12 remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 u64 no/one-arg state-free typed direct-call ABI starts unsigned integer state removal for direct-call thunks that never need runtime state. No-arg u64 constant and boundary return thunks now emit `static TZrUInt64 zr_aot_typed_u64_fn_N(void)` and are called as `zr_aot_typed_u64_fn_N()`. One-arg u64 identity, constant arithmetic, and constant bitwise thunks now emit `static TZrUInt64 zr_aot_typed_u64_fn_N(TZrUInt64 zr_aot_arg0)` and are called with the u64 scalar local only. The same slice fixes two scalar-local support gaps exposed by the u64 smoke: signed-const fallback now reads/writes i64 scalar locals when available, and forced stack-copy prefers the source-local type so u64 call-argument slots keep `zr_aot_uN` instead of stale `zr_aot_sN`. This leaves u64 two/three-arg state-free ABI, f64/bool ABI parity, full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, performance counters, and complete 07-S5 acceptance open.

Setup byte-frame sizing is now aligned with the MethodInfo descriptor rule for the 07-S4 scalar case. `backend_aot_write_c_frame_setup()` computes byte-frame setup requirements from inline-struct frame slots only, and pure scalar generated C omits the `zr_aot_frame_byte_size` and `zr_aot_frame_byte_slot_count` locals entirely when the computed byte-frame requirement is zero. The value SemIR generated summary uses the same inline-struct-only byte-frame calculation, so focused pure scalar output records `value SemIR lowering frameByteSize=0` instead of the raw archived frame layout size. This byte-size rule is independent from the frame-descriptor proof below; inline-struct value-frame functions still keep the byte-slot prologue when their computed requirement is nonzero.

The focused 07-S4 scalar prologue can now omit the generated-frame descriptor itself when the function body is proven frame-free. `backend_aot_c_frame_descriptor.*` centralizes the conservative proof used by `backend_aot_write_c_function_body()`: export publication, frame cleanup, exception handlers, missing ExecIR, unsupported opcodes, or any scalar/value-SemIR fallback that still emits `frame.` keep the descriptor. The current proof accepts only already frame-free scalar SemIR blocks, immediate scalar constants that can skip value-slot writes, scalar-local-only stack copies, direct jumps and scalar-local branch predicates, and scalar-local i64 returns. `backend_aot_write_c_frame_setup()` now receives `includeFrameDescriptor` and computes `includeStackFrameSetup = includeFrameDescriptor || frameByteSize > 0u`; focused pure scalar generated C no longer declares `ZrAotGeneratedFrame frame`, assigns descriptor fields, resolves `ZrAotGeneratedModuleContext`, emits stack frame setup locals, calls `ZrCore_Function_CheckStackAndGc`, or null-fills native frame slots. Functions with value-type inline frame slots, exports, cleanup, exceptions, or unresolved frame users still keep the full descriptor/context/stack setup path.

Generated AOT C root/export returns now publish module exports directly in generated code instead of calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PublishModuleExports(state, &frame)`. `ZrAotGeneratedFrame` carries the active `module`, `moduleExecuted` flag, function table, and generated thunk table from frame setup. `backend_aot_write_c_publish_exports()` emits `zr_aot_publish_exports_direct`, validates `frame.module`, `frame.moduleExecuted`, `frame.function`, and `frame.slotBase`, iterates `frame.function->exportedVariables`, reads each value from `frame.slotBase + export.stackSlot`, copies non-callable values directly, constructs callable export `SZrClosureNative` values directly from metadata and generated thunk pointers, binds captured values from frame/native/VM closure sources when available, calls `ZrCore_Module_AddPubExport` or `ZrCore_Module_AddProExport`, and finally sets `*frame.moduleExecuted = ZR_TRUE`. Generated modules now include `zr_vm_core/module.h` and `zr_vm_common/zr_ast_constants.h` for the direct publication loop. The checked C backend no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PublishModuleExports(state, &frame)` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_MaterializeModuleExportValue(...)`, and the stale public export-materialization wrapper was removed from the active AOT runtime API.

Generated AOT C no longer depends on a `.codex`-local verification copy of its module ABI. `zr_vm_common/include/zr_vm_common/zr_aot_abi.h` is now the public include-tree contract for generated modules and the runtime loader. It defines `ZR_VM_AOT_ABI_VERSION`, `EZrAotBackendKind`, `EZrAotInputKind`, `FZrAotEntryThunk`, `ZrAotCompiledModule`, `FZrVmGetAotCompiledModule`, and `ZR_VM_AOT_EXPORT`, matching the declarations emitted by `backend_aot_c_emitter.c`. `zr_vm_parser/include/zr_vm_parser/writer.h` now also owns `SZrAotWriterOptions` plus the AOT C/LLVM writer entrypoint declarations, so archived backend syntax checks and external writer consumers no longer need a local typedef for the writer options shape. This makes generated C syntax checks use the same public include surface that downstream C compilation must consume.

Primitive constant materialization now has a direct generated-C write path for the immediate scalar subset. `GET_CONSTANT` for null, bool, signed integer, unsigned integer, and float constants emits `zr_aot_value_exec_primitive_constant`, resolves the destination `SZrTypeValue *`, releases any existing owned/GC payload in that slot, and writes the new scalar with `ZrCore_Value_ResetAsNull` or `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET(zr_aot_destination, ...)`. It no longer builds a temporary `zr_aot_constant` and copies it into the destination with `ZrCore_Value_Copy`. `SET_CONSTANT` in generated AOT C now emits `zr_aot_value_exec_set_constant` and writes `*zr_aot_constant = *zr_aot_source`, matching the interpreter's current raw constant-table assignment instead of calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetConstant`. Resolved callable constants and zero-capture `CREATE_CLOSURE` opcodes still construct native closures directly from metadata and generated thunk pointers. Zero-capture `GET_SUB_FUNCTION` child functions now emit only `zr_aot_value_get_sub_function_native_closure_boundary` plus `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD(ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetSubFunctionNativeClosure(..., zr_aot_fn_N))`; the helper validates owner/child metadata, releases the destination, allocates and initializes `SZrClosureNative`, installs the generated thunk and AOT shim metadata, and preserves callable provenance for the destination only on that direct path. Unresolved callable `GET_CONSTANT` materialization emits `zr_aot_value_unsupported_callable_constant_materialization`, validates the source constant and destination slot, checks callable metadata, reports `unsupported AOT callable constant materialization`, and fails through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` instead of calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CopyConstant`. Captured or unresolved `CREATE_CLOSURE` now emits `zr_aot_value_unsupported_create_closure_materialization`, records `zr_aot_capture_count`, validates the source/destination/metadata boundary, reports `unsupported AOT CREATE_CLOSURE materialization`, clears callable provenance for that destination, and fails explicitly instead of calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CreateClosure`. Captured, unresolved, or missing `GET_SUB_FUNCTION` child closures emit `zr_aot_value_unsupported_get_sub_function_materialization`, record the child capture count when known, report `unsupported AOT GET_SUB_FUNCTION materialization`, clear callable provenance, and fail explicitly instead of calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetSubFunction`. Plain non-immediate constants still follow the direct constant-table `ZrCore_Value_Copy` path; LLVM keeps its old helper routes until parity and real captured-closure materialization are handled.

The focused M2 scalar-local path extends immediate primitive constants with destination-local mirrors. `backend_aot_write_c_direct_primitive_constant()` receives `functionIr`, writes the existing frame-slot `SZrTypeValue`, then checks scalar-local coverage and mirrors bool/i64/u64/f64 immediates into `zr_aot_bN`, `zr_aot_sN`, `zr_aot_uN`, or `zr_aot_fN` when the constant payload type matches the declared local kind. The typed-scalar generated product now locks signed and float mirrors such as `zr_aot_s0 = (TZrInt64)21;`, `zr_aot_s6 = (TZrInt64)9;`, `zr_aot_f19 = (TZrFloat64)1.5;`, and `zr_aot_f20 = (TZrFloat64)2;`. Current `uint` literals in the focused source still materialize first as signed `INT64` constants, and the 07-S2 u64 constant/conversion slice now recognizes that lowered shape: when a signed immediate targets a slot with u64 scalar-local coverage, the backend can write `zr_aot_uN = (TZrUInt64)literal`, record the write as u64, and keep the following `TO_UINT` / u64 binary chain on C locals such as `zr_aot_u6 = (TZrUInt64)zr_aot_s6;`, `zr_aot_u7 = (TZrUInt64)4;`, and `zr_aot_u8 = zr_aot_u6 + zr_aot_u7;`. The 07-S2 u64 binary result local-only slice extends that chain from source reuse to destination materialization removal: when every reachable later consumer can read the u64 scalar local, the `unsignedSum` binary block emits only `zr_aot_u8 = zr_aot_u6 + zr_aot_u7;` and no longer constructs a `SZrTypeValue *` destination, `zr_aot_u_result`, or a `frame.slotBase[8]` result write.

The following 07-S2 i64 primitive constant cross-block local-only slice applies the reachable-consumer proof to focused entry constants. Slots 0 and 1 now emit only `zr_aot_s0 = (TZrInt64)21;` and `zr_aot_s1 = (TZrInt64)2;` without immediately materializing the same payload through `zr_aot_value_exec_primitive_constant` and `frame.slotBase[0/1].value`. The proof remains conservative at `FUNCTION_RETURN`: because current direct-return lowering reads the frame result slot, return-value slots are still materialized before the direct-return block until that boundary becomes scalar-local aware.

The following 07-S2 f64 primitive constant local-only slice extends the same standalone constant pattern to focused float constants. Slots 19 and 20 now emit `zr_aot_scalar_constant_f64_local` blocks with `zr_aot_f19 = (TZrFloat64)1.5;` and `zr_aot_f20 = (TZrFloat64)2;`, then the f64 binary consumes those locals directly without the old double payload materialization through `frame.slotBase[19/20].value`.

The following 07-S2 u64 bitwise result local-only slice applies the same result-skip proof to `unsignedMasked`, so its block emits only `zr_aot_u12 = zr_aot_u8 & zr_aot_u7;` without destination pointer, result temporary, or `frame.slotBase[12]` materialization.

The following 07-S2 u64 shift result local-only slice applies that proof to `unsignedShifted` and `unsignedShiftedBack`. Their blocks keep the signed shift-count range guard, then emit only `zr_aot_u13 = zr_aot_u8 << zr_aot_s1;` or `zr_aot_u14 = zr_aot_u10 >> zr_aot_s1;` without destination pointer, result temporary, or `frame.slotBase[13/14]` materialization.

The following 07-S2 u64 bit-not result local-only slice applies that proof to `unsignedInverted`, so its block emits only `zr_aot_u33 = ~zr_aot_u7;` without destination pointer, result temporary, or `frame.slotBase[33]` materialization.

The focused M2 branch path now distinguishes proven slot/slot predicates from unproven slot/constant predicates. For the straight-line `if (product > threshold)` / `JUMP_IF_LESS_EQUAL_SIGNED` shape, both operands are written earlier in the same basic block, so generated C can use the maintained `zr_aot_s2` / `zr_aot_s4` locals directly. After the 07-S2 cross-block must-write proof, the later `if (product == 42)` / `JUMP_IF_NOT_EQUAL_SIGNED_CONST` shape can also use `zr_aot_s2` when every reachable predecessor has written it, so generated C emits `if (zr_aot_s2 != zr_aot_right_literal) {` without a left `SZrTypeValue` source. Resume/deopt local restoration and full C-local authoritative storage remain later AOT work.

Closure capture access now uses explicit AOT runtime boundaries for `GET_CLOSURE`, `SET_CLOSURE`, `GETUPVAL`, and `SETUPVAL`. `GET_CLOSURE` / `GETUPVAL` emit `zr_aot_value_exec_get_closure_value` and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetClosureValue(state, &frame, destinationSlot, closureIndex)`; `SET_CLOSURE` / `SETUPVAL` emit `zr_aot_value_exec_set_closure_value` and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetClosureValue(state, &frame, sourceSlot, closureIndex)`. The helpers resolve the active closure capture, handle native and VM closures, copy values, and apply setter barriers centrally. Generated C no longer expands current-closure stack lookup, native/VM closure decoding, capture-value read/write, direct copy, or barrier templates for these opcodes. The generated-C smoke is compile-only for this hand-built opcode fixture; executing real captured closure AOT paths remains tied to captured-closure materialization and direct call work. LLVM parity remains future work.

Ownership opcode lowering now has direct generated-C core calls for `OWN_UNIQUE`, `OWN_BORROW`, `OWN_LOAN`, `OWN_SHARE`, `OWN_WEAK`, `OWN_DETACH`, `OWN_UPGRADE`, and `OWN_RELEASE`. Generated C emits `zr_aot_value_exec_ownership_core` for copy-like ownership operations, validates `state`, `frame.function`, `frame.slotBase`, and `frame.generatedFrameSlotCount`, resolves destination/source `SZrTypeValue` operands with `ZrCore_Stack_GetValue(frame.slotBase + slot)`, then calls `ZrCore_Ownership_UniqueValue`, `BorrowValue`, `LoanValue`, `ShareValue`, `WeakValue`, `DetachValue`, or `UpgradeValue` directly. Failed ownership transfer resets the destination with `ZrCore_Value_ResetAsNull`, matching the old wrapper behavior without preserving the instruction-helper call boundary. `OWN_RELEASE` emits `zr_aot_value_exec_ownership_release`, calls `ZrCore_Ownership_ReleaseValue(state, zr_aot_source)`, and resets the destination slot to null. The C backend no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Own*` for these ownership opcodes; LLVM parity and source-level executable ownership fixtures remain future work.

Super-array integer opcodes now lower in generated AOT C through direct core fast semantic boundaries instead of instruction helper wrappers. `SUPER_ARRAY_GET_INT`, `SUPER_ARRAY_GET_INT_PLAIN_DEST`, `SUPER_ARRAY_SET_INT`, `SUPER_ARRAY_ADD_INT`, `SUPER_ARRAY_ADD_INT4`, `SUPER_ARRAY_ADD_INT4_CONST`, and `SUPER_ARRAY_FILL_INT4_CONST` are routed through `backend_aot_c_lowering_super_array.c`, resolve stack slots from `frame.slotBase`, validate signed integer operands and constants, then call the fast core APIs declared in `zr_vm_core/object.h`: `ZrCore_Object_SuperArrayTryGetIntFast`, `TrySetIntFast`, `AddIntAssumeFast`, `AddIntDiscardResultAssumeFast`, `AddInt4ConstAssumeFast`, and `FillInt4ConstAssumeFast`. The generated path deliberately avoids the generic `ZrCore_Object_SuperArrayGetInt` / `SetInt` / `AddInt` wrappers because those may fall back to dynamic member/index behavior. Non-fast or malformed shapes report `unsupported AOT super-array integer fast path` and fail through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` instead of emitting `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SuperArray*`; LLVM parity and broader dynamic super-array lowering remain future work.

Iterator opcodes now lower in generated AOT C through direct core iterator boundaries instead of instruction helper wrappers. `ITER_INIT`, `DYN_ITER_INIT`, `ITER_MOVE_NEXT`, `DYN_ITER_MOVE_NEXT`, `ITER_CURRENT`, and `SUPER_DYN_ITER_MOVE_NEXT_JUMP_IF_FALSE` are routed through `backend_aot_c_lowering_iterators.c`, resolve iterator/source/destination stack slots from `frame.slotBase`, then call `ZrCore_Object_IterInit`, the cached array fast path `ZrCore_Object_TryIterMoveNextCachedArrayFast`, fallback `ZrCore_Object_IterMoveNext`, the cached current fast path `ZrCore_Object_TryIterCurrentCachedMemberFastStackResult`, or fallback `ZrCore_Object_IterCurrent` directly. The fused move-next false branch validates the result as bool and emits the generated `goto` directly, so it no longer routes through `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_IsTruthy`. Unsupported iterator shapes report `unsupported AOT iterator core path` or `unsupported AOT iterator branch result` and fail through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` instead of emitting `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Iter*`; LLVM parity and broader source-level iterator execution fixtures remain future work.

Scope lifecycle opcodes now lower in generated AOT C through direct frame, stack, and closure core operations. `MARK_TO_BE_CLOSED` emits `zr_aot_scope_mark_to_be_closed`, validates `frame.slotBase` and the generated-frame slot count, then calls `ZrCore_Closure_ToBeClosedValueClosureNew(state, frame.slotBase + slot)`. `CLOSE_SCOPE` emits `zr_aot_scope_close_scope`, preserves `state->stackTop` with `ZrCore_Stack_SavePointerAsOffset` and `ZrCore_Stack_LoadOffsetToPointer`, raises stack top to the active call frame top when needed, then closes pending scope registrations with `ZrCore_Closure_CloseStackValue` and `ZrCore_Closure_CloseRegisteredValues` directly in generated C. The C backend no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_MarkToBeClosed` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CloseScope` for these opcodes; LLVM parity remains helper-backed until that backend receives the same direct-core contract.

Dynamic/meta value access now has an explicit generated-C failure boundary for `META_GET`, `META_SET`, `SUPER_META_GET_CACHED`, `SUPER_META_SET_CACHED`, `SUPER_META_GET_STATIC_CACHED`, and `SUPER_META_SET_STATIC_CACHED`. Generated C emits `zr_aot_value_unsupported_meta_value_access`, materializes the primary stack operand, secondary stack operand, and member/cache index, reports `unsupported AOT meta value access` with `ZrCore_Debug_RunError`, and exits through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` instead of calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Meta*` instruction helpers. This records object/meta member access as an unsupported dynamic boundary until real generated meta value access and meta dispatch semantics are specified. LLVM keeps its old helper routes until parity is handled.

Meta-call opcodes now also have an explicit generated-C unsupported boundary. `SUPER_META_CALL_NO_ARGS`, `SUPER_META_CALL_CACHED`, `SUPER_META_TAIL_CALL_NO_ARGS`, `SUPER_META_TAIL_CALL_CACHED`, `META_CALL`, and `META_TAIL_CALL` route through `backend_aot_write_c_unsupported_meta_call()`, which emits `zr_aot_unsupported_meta_call`, records destination, receiver, and argument count slots, validates the generated frame slots, reports `unsupported AOT meta call`, and exits through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()`. The C backend no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareMetaCall`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CallPreparedOrGeneric`, or `ZrAotGeneratedDirectCall zr_aot_direct_call` for these meta-call bytecodes. Real generated meta dispatch remains a future contract; this slice prevents it from being hidden behind the old prepared-call helper route.

Unsupported generated-instruction paths now use an explicit cleanup-exit runtime boundary. Invalid branch targets, default opcode lowering paths, dispatch-loop fallthrough, and generated function fallthrough route through `backend_aot_write_c_unsupported_instruction()` / `_expr()`, emit a `zr_aot_unsupported_instruction` marker with function index, instruction index, and opcode metadata, and exit through `ZR_AOT_C_RETURN(ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReportUnsupportedInstruction(...))`. Generated C no longer expands instruction/opcode locals, hand-written `unsupported AOT instruction` `RunError` text, or a local `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` block for this boundary. Unsupported opcodes remain unsupported, but their reporting is centralized in the AOT runtime helper.

Generated AOT C instruction-entry bookkeeping is now treated as a historical direct-frame boundary, not as typed hot-path code. The `backend_aot_write_c_begin_instruction()` helper still exists in the control lowering source, but 07-S1 removes the call from `backend_aot_c_function_body.c`, so focused typed scalar products no longer contain `zr_aot_begin_instruction` or per-instruction observation publication. The C backend still avoids `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_BeginInstruction` from `backend_aot_c*.c`; later 07 slices own MethodInfo/observation policy convergence and LLVM parity.

Pending control transfer opcodes now lower through generated C control-flow blocks instead of instruction helper wrappers. `SET_PENDING_RETURN`, `SET_PENDING_BREAK`, and `SET_PENDING_CONTINUE` route through `backend_aot_write_c_pending_control_transfer()`, emit `zr_aot_pending_return` / `zr_aot_pending_break` / `zr_aot_pending_continue` markers, validate the active generated frame, optionally resolve the pending return value from `frame.slotBase`, call `execution_set_pending_control`, then either resume an outer finally with `execution_resume_pending_via_outer_finally` or jump to the target instruction with `execution_jump_to_instruction_offset`. The block refreshes `frame.callInfo`, `frame.slotBase`, `state->callInfoList`, and `state->stackTop`, recomputes `zr_aot_next_instruction` from the active program counter, and dispatches inside the generated function. The C backend no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetPendingReturn`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetPendingBreak`, or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetPendingContinue` from `backend_aot_c*.c`; LLVM parity and full generated control/exception execution fixtures remain separate work.

`TRY` and `END_TRY` now keep generated control markers but delegate exception-handler stack details to AOT runtime boundary helpers. `TRY` emits `zr_aot_try_direct` plus `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Try(state, &frame, handlerIndex)`, and `END_TRY` emits `zr_aot_end_try_direct` plus `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_EndTry(state, &frame, handlerIndex)`. The helpers own handler index validation, active `SZrCallInfo` recovery, handler push or END_TRY handler lookup/finally-phase/pop behavior, and success-path refresh of `frame.callInfo`, `frame.slotBase`, `state->callInfoList`, and `state->stackTop`. Generated C no longer expands `execution_push_exception_handler`, `execution_find_handler_state`, `frame.function->exceptionHandlerList[...]`, `handlerState->phase = ZR_VM_EXCEPTION_HANDLER_PHASE_FINALLY`, or TRY/END_TRY-specific generated `RunError` templates in those blocks.

`CATCH` now keeps the generated `zr_aot_catch_direct` marker but delegates exception materialization to `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Catch(state, &frame, destinationSlot)`. The runtime helper validates the destination stack slot, resolves it with `ZrCore_Stack_GetValue`, copies `state->currentException` into the destination and clears it when present, writes null when no current exception exists, and clears pending control. Generated C no longer expands the destination `SZrTypeValue *`, generated CATCH slot diagnostics, `ZrCore_Value_Copy(state, zr_aot_destination, &state->currentException)`, `ZrCore_Exception_ClearCurrent(state)`, or `ZrCore_Value_ResetAsNull(zr_aot_destination)` in that block.

`THROW` now keeps the generated `zr_aot_throw_direct` marker but delegates exception normalization and in-frame unwind dispatch to `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Throw(state, &frame, sourceSlot, &zr_aot_next_instruction)`. Generated C initializes `zr_aot_next_instruction`, guards the helper result, and jumps to the generated dispatch loop only when the helper returns a concrete resume instruction. The runtime helper owns payload slot validation, pending-control cleanup, payload normalization, current-frame unwind/refresh, resume-index calculation, and unhandled-exception propagation through `ZrCore_Exception_Throw`. Generated C no longer expands `SZrTypeValue` source/payload locals, `ZrCore_Exception_NormalizeThrownValue`, `execution_unwind_exception_to_handler`, or the THROW-specific generated diagnostics in that block.

`END_FINALLY` now keeps the generated `zr_aot_end_finally_direct` marker but delegates finally exit and pending-control resume behavior to `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_EndFinally(state, &frame, handlerIndex, &zr_aot_next_instruction)`. Generated C initializes `zr_aot_next_instruction`, guards the helper result, and jumps to the generated dispatch loop only when the helper returns a concrete resume instruction. The runtime helper owns handler pop, pending exception unwind, unhandled pending-exception propagation through `ZrCore_Exception_Throw`, pending return/break/continue resume, pending return-value copy, pending-control cleanup, frame refresh, and resume-index calculation. Generated C no longer expands the END_FINALLY `switch (state->pendingControl.kind)`, `resumeCallInfo`, `handlerState`, `targetSlot`, pending return-value copy, unwind, frame-refresh, or resume-index template in that block. `SET_PENDING_RETURN`, `SET_PENDING_BREAK`, and `SET_PENDING_CONTINUE` still use their earlier generated pending-control transfer blocks until a later 07-S5 slice centralizes them.

Root/export `FUNCTION_RETURN` now separates module export publication from the return instruction. When the root generated function has exported variables, generated C emits `zr_aot_publish_exports_direct` before the same `zr_aot_direct_return` block used by non-export returns. Export publication is now a generated loop with direct value copy or direct native-closure construction for callable exports; unsupported captured export shapes fail explicitly with `unsupported AOT module export closure capture materialization`. `FUNCTION_RETURN` no longer falls back to `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Return(state, &frame, ..., ZR_TRUE)`. The direct return block still performs handler discard, return escape metadata, captured stack-value close, result copy, and caller stack-top restoration.

Global object reads now use an explicit runtime boundary in `backend_aot_c_lowering_values.c`. `GET_GLOBAL` emits the `zr_aot_value_exec_get_global` marker and calls `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetGlobal(state, &frame, destinationSlot)` through `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD`; the runtime helper resolves the destination frame slot, checks and copies `state->global->zrObject` when it is an object, and resets the destination to null otherwise. Generated C no longer expands `zr_aot_global_object`, direct global type checks, direct `ZrCore_Value_Copy`, or direct destination null reset for `GET_GLOBAL`. LLVM parity remains separate.

Runtime type reflection now also uses an explicit runtime boundary. `TYPEOF` emits `zr_aot_value_exec_typeof` and calls `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_TypeOf(state, &frame, destinationSlot, sourceSlot)` through `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD`; the runtime helper resolves source/destination frame slots, invokes `ZrCore_Reflection_TypeOfValue`, and reports failure centrally. Generated C no longer expands direct source/destination `SZrTypeValue` lookup or direct `ZrCore_Reflection_TypeOfValue(state, zr_aot_source, zr_aot_destination)` for `TYPEOF`. LLVM parity remains separate.

Runtime object/struct conversion opcodes now use an explicit runtime boundary. `TO_OBJECT` and `TO_STRUCT` emit `zr_aot_value_exec_to_object` / `zr_aot_value_exec_to_struct` and call `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ToObject(state, &frame, destinationSlot, sourceSlot, typeNameConstantIndex)` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ToStruct(state, &frame, destinationSlot, sourceSlot, typeNameConstantIndex)` through `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD`; the runtime helpers resolve destination/source frame slots, validate the type-name constant, invoke `ZrCore_Execution_ToObject` / `ZrCore_Execution_ToStruct`, and report failure centrally. Generated C no longer expands direct destination/source `SZrTypeValue` lookup, direct `frame.function->constantValueList[index]` type-name lookup, or direct `ZrCore_Execution_ToObject/ToStruct(state, frame.callInfo, ...)` for these opcodes. Full inline struct boxing/unboxing from frame byte spans and LLVM parity remain separate contracts.

The legacy quickened integer arithmetic family now has its own generated-C lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_legacy_int_arithmetic.c`. `ADD_INT`, `ADD_INT_CONST`, `SUB_INT`, and `SUB_INT_CONST` read legacy `SZrTypeValue` stack slots, validate signed/unsigned integer operands, and emit direct C expressions such as `zr_aot_left_int + zr_aot_right_int`, `zr_aot_left_int + zr_aot_right_literal`, `zr_aot_left_int - zr_aot_right_int`, and `zr_aot_left_int - zr_aot_right_literal`. Const forms read the right operand from the function constant table and format signed, unsigned, or bool integer-like constants as `TZrInt64` C literals. Missing or unsupported constants now emit `unsupported AOT ADD_INT_CONST constant` / `unsupported AOT SUB_INT_CONST constant` and fail through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` instead of falling back to `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_AddIntConst`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SubInt`, or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SubIntConst`.

Generic numeric arithmetic now has a generated-C boundary-helper lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_generic_numeric_arithmetic.c`. Generic `ADD`, `SUB`, `MUL`, `DIV`, `MOD`, and `NEG` keep only `zr_aot_arith_exec_generic_numeric_binary_boundary` / `zr_aot_arith_exec_generic_numeric_unary_boundary` markers and call `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GenericNumericAdd/Sub/Mul/Div/Mod/Neg()` through `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD`. The generated C no longer expands destination/left/right `SZrTypeValue *` locals, runtime numeric tag branches, direct `+`, `-`, `*`, `/`, `%`, `fmod(...)`, unary `-`, or generated zero-guard failure blocks. `aot_runtime_values.c` owns the primitive numeric semantics for this dynamic boundary: it validates frame slots, accepts only numeric operands, chooses float, signed integer, or unsigned integer extraction, preserves `divide by zero` / `modulo by zero` failures, runs generic float `MOD` with `fmod(leftFloat, rightFloat)`, writes the destination through `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET`, and reports `unsupported AOT generic numeric arithmetic` for nonnumeric, string, dynamic/meta, or unsupported bool-as-numeric cases. String concatenation and meta arithmetic therefore remain explicit unsupported/dynamic boundaries until typed SemIR/call lowering gives them a non-helper AOT contract.

Focused 2026-06-22 07-S5 generic numeric scalar-local sync validation extends those helper boundaries with post-helper local restoration. The generic numeric emitters now receive the current function IR and share a sync helper that emits `zr_aot_generic_numeric_sync_i64_local_boundary`, `zr_aot_generic_numeric_sync_u64_local_boundary`, or `zr_aot_generic_numeric_sync_f64_local_boundary` plus `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SyncSignedIntLocal()`, `SyncUnsignedIntLocal()`, or `SyncFloatLocal()` when the helper-written destination is a matching scalar local. Source contracts lock the helperized `GenericNumeric*` call shape, function-body `functionIr` routing, and all three sync helpers; the existing float `MOD` smoke continues to validate generated shared-library compileability for the boundary helper path.

Generic primitive conversions now have a generated-C boundary-helper lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_generic_conversion.c`. Generic `TO_BOOL`, `TO_INT`, `TO_UINT`, and `TO_FLOAT` route through `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ConvertGenericToBool/Int/UInt/Float()` instead of expanding direct generated tag-branch ladders or printing broader `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ToBool`, `ToInt`, `ToUInt`, or `ToFloat` calls. The generated C keeps only conversion markers and helper guards; the dedicated runtime helpers preserve the old primitive-only null/bool/signed/unsigned/float conversion semantics and report `unsupported AOT generic primitive conversion` for non-primitive, object/string, dynamic/meta, and other unsupported cases.

Generic primitive truthiness now has a generated-C boundary-helper lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_generic_logical.c`. Generic `LOGICAL_NOT` and generic `JUMP_IF` keep the existing `zr_aot_generic_logical_*` markers and call `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GenericPrimitiveLogicalNot()` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GenericPrimitiveIsTruthy()` instead of expanding generated null/bool/signed/unsigned/float branch ladders or calling the broader `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_LogicalNot` / `IsTruthy` helpers. The dedicated runtime helpers preserve the old primitive truthiness semantics, `LOGICAL_NOT` synchronizes any bool scalar local through `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SyncBoolLocal()` rather than generated destination-slot decoding, and string/object/meta/dynamic truthiness remains an explicit `unsupported AOT generic primitive truthiness` boundary.

Generic primitive equality now lives in the same logical boundary-helper module. Generic `LOGICAL_EQUAL` and `LOGICAL_NOT_EQUAL` keep generated markers and helper guards, then call `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GenericPrimitiveLogicalEqual()` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GenericPrimitiveLogicalNotEqual()` instead of expanding generated primitive equality branches or falling back to the broader `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_LogicalEqual` / `LogicalNotEqual` dynamic helpers. The runtime helpers own same-runtime-type checks, null/bool/signed/unsigned/float comparison, normalized bool payload comparison, bool destination writes, and `unsupported AOT generic primitive equality` failures; generated C only performs required bool scalar-local resynchronization through the `zr_aot_generic_logical_sync_bool_local_boundary` + `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SyncBoolLocal()` boundary after the helper returns.

The bool binary `LOGICAL_AND` and `LOGICAL_OR` bytecode opcodes now also have direct generated-C lowering in `backend_aot_c_lowering_generic_logical.c`. When those opcodes are present, generated C validates both operands are bool values, normalizes `nativeBool` payloads, emits `zr_aot_left_bool && zr_aot_right_bool` or `zr_aot_left_bool || zr_aot_right_bool`, and writes a bool destination directly. Unsupported non-bool operands report `unsupported AOT bool logical binary` and fail through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` rather than calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_LogicalAnd` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_LogicalOr`. Focused 2026-06-22 07-S5 scalar-local validation adds an opcode-level local-only path: if bool scalar-local analysis proves both operands have already been written to `zr_aot_bN` and the bool destination can skip its value slot, generated C emits `zr_aot_bool_binary_scalar_local` and writes the destination bool local directly. The old `zr_aot_bool_logical_and` / `zr_aot_bool_logical_or` frame-slot fallback remains for unproven operands or destinations. Source-level `&&` / `||` still normally lowers to short-circuit branch CFG before `LOGICAL_AND` / `LOGICAL_OR`; the source-level shared-library smoke therefore validates branch behavior, while the logical source-contract test locks the bytecode direct-emitter shape.

Typed string equality now has its first direct generated-C lowering in the same logical module. `LOGICAL_EQUAL_STRING` and `LOGICAL_NOT_EQUAL_STRING` validate string operands, cast the payloads with `ZR_CAST_STRING`, read byte lengths and native byte pointers through `ZrCore_String_GetByteLength` / `ZrCore_String_GetNativeString`, compare equal-length byte spans with `memcmp`, and write bool destinations with `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET` when the destination still needs a value-slot write. Focused 2026-06-22 07-S5 scalar-local validation adds a bool-result local-only path: when scalar-local analysis proves the string equality bool destination can skip its value slot, generated C emits `zr_aot_string_logical_bool_scalar_local`, reuses the same string comparison body, and writes `zr_aot_bN` directly instead of materializing `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination` or calling `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET` for that result. Unsupported operands or null string objects report `unsupported AOT string equality` and fail through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` rather than calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_LogicalEqualString`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_LogicalNotEqualString`, or `ZrCore_String_Equal`. Generated modules now emit `#include "zr_vm_core/string.h"` and `#include <string.h>` so downstream C compilation sees the string accessors and byte comparison function. LLVM string equality still keeps its existing helper route until LLVM parity is handled.

The generated-frame ABI is still mixed during this migration: inline struct payloads are addressed as byte spans from `frame.slotBase`, while scalar temporaries are still addressed as legacy stack value slots with `ZrCore_Stack_GetValue(frame.slotBase + slot)`. Typed call/return lowering is executable only for the first proven POD direct-call subset; large hidden returns, whole non-POD drop/finalization, mismatched nested inline struct field transfer, generated meta-call execution, and tail-call overlap remain future slices. The current AOT behavior for proven-but-unsupported value fields is an explicit generated failure boundary rather than helper fallback.

Dynamic, generic, and static resolved function calls now have direct generated-C core-call paths for the existing stack-call ABI. `backend_aot_c_function_body.c` finds the AotExecIR row for the current bytecode instruction and treats `ZR_SEMIR_OPCODE_DYN_CALL` / `ZR_SEMIR_OPCODE_DYN_TAIL_CALL` as dynamic even when quickening has rewritten the bytecode opcode to a generic `FUNCTION_CALL` / `FUNCTION_TAIL_CALL` family opcode. Static resolved callsites still win and use `zr_aot_direct_static_function_call`; generated C resolves callee metadata from the callable slot with `ZrCore_Closure_GetMetadataFunctionFromValue`, stages callable and arguments at the caller frame-storage top, prepares the resolved VM call frame with `ZrCore_Function_PreCallPreparedResolvedVmFunctionWithArgumentSource`, invokes the known generated thunk `zr_aot_fn_N`, posts the call through `ZrCore_Function_PostCall`, and refreshes `frame.callInfo` / `frame.slotBase` from the active caller frame. Required scalar-local restoration after a static direct call is now a runtime boundary: generated C emits `zr_aot_direct_static_function_call_sync_i64_local_boundary` / `zr_aot_direct_static_function_call_sync_bool_local_boundary` plus `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SyncSignedIntLocal()` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SyncBoolLocal()`, rather than expanding a `zr_aot_direct_call_result` stack lookup and tag-specific payload read in the generated function. `SyncBoolLocal()` intentionally preserves the previous generated behavior by leaving the bool local unchanged when the source slot is not bool. The staged window keeps call setup out of caller inline payload bytes, while the argument-source frame parameters keep byte-backed VALUE arguments copyable from their original layout slots. Dynamic and unresolved generic function calls are emitted by the shared C template in `backend_aot_write_c_core_function_call()`. The template validates frame slots, anchors the callable and destination slots with `ZrCore_Function_StackAnchorInit`, sets `state->stackTop.valuePointer = callBase + 1 + argumentCount`, invokes `ZrCore_Function_CallAndRestoreAnchor`, restores the destination anchor, copies the result with `ZrCore_Value_Copy`, and refreshes the active frame. The C backend no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Call(state, &frame, ...)` for dynamic call lowering, no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareDirectCall` for generic direct function calls, and no longer emits `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareStaticDirectCall` / `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_FinishDirectCall` for static resolved direct calls; generated meta-call execution remains a separate boundary.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 call-boundary writer split moves that generic/dynamic/static resolved call boundary ownership into `backend_aot_c_call_boundaries.c`. The new module owns the shared `CallStackValue` writer, the static resolved `CallStaticDirect` writer, and the i64/bool/u64/f64 scalar-local result synchronization markers and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Sync*Local()` helper calls. `backend_aot_c_lowering_calls.c` now keeps unsupported meta-call emission plus the concrete typed direct-call scalar writers, so ordinary typed thunk writers are no longer mixed with VM-call boundary marshaling templates. This is an ownership split only; the generated marker strings and runtime helper calls are preserved.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 value-access boundary writer split moves dynamic/member/index and unsupported meta/dynamic value-access boundary ownership into `backend_aot_c_value_access_boundaries.c`. The new module owns the six concrete dynamic value access runtime-boundary writers plus the two unsupported value-access boundary writers; `backend_aot_c_lowering_values.c` no longer contains those VM boundary marker strings and remains focused on non-boundary value lowering such as constants, materialization, ownership, and `TO_STRING`. RED was global contracts failing 2/7 with `Expected Non-NULL` when they first looked for the missing boundary module. GREEN passed global contracts 7/0, global shared-library smoke 9/0, and source contracts 19/0; `zr_vm_parser_shared` was rebuilt and confirmed `backend_aot_c_value_access_boundaries.c.o` linked into parser shared. After the split, `backend_aot_c_lowering_values.c` is 839 physical / 755 non-empty lines, the new boundary source is 165 / 147, and the global contract file is 703 / 653. This is ownership hardening for existing boundary helpers; full typed ABI, inline structs, in/out writeback, broader deopt/dynamic bridges, full 07-S5 acceptance, and stages 08-12 remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 dynamic/deopt bridge surfacing makes SemIR dynamic calls explicit at the generated AOT C boundary. `backend_aot_write_c_dynamic_function_call()` now takes a `deoptId`, `backend_aot_c_function_body.c` threads the ExecIR SemIR dynamic-call deopt id into generic `FUNCTION_CALL` / no-arg call lowering, and generated C emits `zr_aot_dynamic_deopt_bridge deopt=...` plus `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CallDynamicDeoptBridge(...)`. The runtime helper validates the deopt id when a SemIR deopt table is available and otherwise delegates to `CallStackValue`, so ordinary generic direct calls keep their existing `CallStackValue` path and are not mislabeled as deopt bridges. The focused smoke was split into `tests/parser/test_aot_c_dynamic_deopt_bridge_smoke.c` to keep the existing call shared-library smoke below the large-file threshold. RED was call contracts failing 1/4 on the missing `deoptId`/bridge surface; GREEN passed call contracts 4/0, call shared-library smoke 5/0, dynamic deopt bridge smoke 1/0, source contracts 19/0, global contracts 7/0, and SemIR dynamic call deopt 1/0. This surfaces dynamic call deopt identity but still leaves full typed ABI, inline structs, in/out writeback, broader dynamic value-access hardening, complete 07-S5 acceptance, and stages 08-12 open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 dynamic value-access deopt bridge surfacing applies the same explicit deopt identity to dynamic member and index runtime boundaries. The six `backend_aot_write_c_direct_*member*` / `*_by_index` writers now take a `deoptId`, emit `zr_aot_value_dynamic_deopt_bridge deopt=...`, and call `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ValidateDynamicDeoptBridge(state, &frame, deoptId, ...)` immediately before the existing `GetMember`, `SetMember`, `GetMemberSlot`, `SetMemberSlot`, `GetByIndex`, or `SetByIndex` helper. `backend_aot_c_function_body.c` looks up the current ExecIR row to pass the SemIR deopt id for generic member/index opcodes and uses the NONE sentinel when no visible deopt row exists. `CallDynamicDeoptBridge` now reuses the same validation helper, while member/index semantics stay in the original runtime helpers. RED was global contracts failing 1/7 on the missing validation helper and value-access marker; GREEN passed global contracts 7/0, dynamic deopt bridge smoke 2/0, source contracts 19/0, global shared-library smoke 9/0, SemIR dynamic member deopt 1/0, and SemIR dynamic index deopt 1/0. This closes the current broader dynamic value-access hardening item for deopt surfacing, but full typed ABI, inline structs, in/out writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, and stages 08-12 remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 boundary guardrail allowlist hardening makes the M1.5 acceptance classifier explicit about the VM/native boundaries that are still permitted while typed lowering is being converged. `tests/parser/test_aot_c_guardrail_contracts.c` now accepts scalar and inline-struct typed return helpers, `Sync*Local` result writeback helpers, `CallStackValue`, `CallStaticDirect`, `CallInlineStruct`, `CallDynamicDeoptBridge`, `ValidateDynamicDeoptBridge`, and the dynamic member/index `Get*` / `Set*` helpers. The same guardrail continues to reject unclassified VM fallback calls such as `ZrCore_Stack_GetValue`, `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET`, and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Add`. RED was guardrail contracts failing 1/4 when the new allowed boundary helpers were not classified; GREEN passed guardrail contracts 4/0 plus source contracts 19/0, global contracts 7/0, return contracts 1/0, call contracts 4/0, typed-call contracts 4/0, and dynamic deopt bridge smoke 2/0. This is acceptance hardening only and does not change generated C behavior; full typed ABI, inline structs, in/out writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, and stages 08-12 remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 MethodInfo typed return signature validation fills the generated signature gap for script-level i64 typed scalar returns. `backend_aot_c_emitter.c` now passes `SZrAotExecIrFunction` into signature emission; when callable return metadata is absent, it scans `FUNCTION_RETURN` instructions and requires every return to pass `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_can_direct_return_i64_local(...)` before synthesizing an i64 `SZrFunctionTypedTypeRef`. The generated typed scalar product now emits `returnType = &zr_aot_signature_0_types[0]`, `hasReturnValue = 1`, and i64 `baseType/staticCType` rows instead of a null return signature. RED was typed scalar generated-product failing 1/1 on the missing return pointer. GREEN passed typed scalar 1/0, frame setup contracts 1/0, source contracts 19/0, and return contracts 1/0; 07§9 environment and SZrValue/double-write greps on generated typed scalar remained empty. This closed only the i64 script-level MethodInfo return metadata gap at that point; full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, and stages 08-12 remained open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 MethodInfo scalar return signature validation extends the script-level inferred signature path to typed-local bool/u64/f64 returns. `backend_aot_c_emitter.c` now uses a generic scalar return scanner and tries i64/bool/u64/f64 in order; every `FUNCTION_RETURN` must satisfy the same scalar-local proof before the generated `SZrAotSignature` receives a non-null `returnType`. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals.c` now centralizes the return proof in `can_return_kind_local`: typed callable direct-return helpers still require callable return metadata, while script signature inference uses bool/u64/f64 helpers without that metadata gate. The new `aot_c_method_info_signature` fixture emits separate bool/u64/f64 generated C files, each with `returnType = &zr_aot_signature_0_types[0]`, `hasReturnValue = 1`, and the expected `baseType/staticCType` row (`1`, `9`, `11`). RED was the focused method-info signature test failing 1/1 on the missing return pointer; GREEN passed method-info signature 1/0 plus frame setup contracts 1/0, source contracts 19/0, return contracts 1/0, typed scalar 1/0, and CTest registration 1/1. This closes the current typed-local bool/u64/f64 script signature gap; expression-direct-return scalarization outside the current proof scope, full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, and stages 08-12 remain open.

Focused 2026-06-24 07-S5 script typed-local return-route validation moves those bool/u64/f64 script returns from the generic frame-slot return boundary to typed native-to-VM return helpers. `backend_aot_c_typed_return.c` still accepts the original direct callable proof, but now also accepts the inferred script proof for bool/u64/f64 when callable return metadata is absent. Generated bool/u64/f64 fixtures now call `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReturnBool(state, zr_aot_b2)`, `ReturnU64(state, zr_aot_u2)`, and `ReturnF64(state, zr_aot_f2)` and no longer contain `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Return(state, &frame, ...)` for those cases. RED was method-info signature 1/1 failing on the missing `ReturnBool` helper; GREEN passed method-info signature 1/0, return contracts 1/0, frame setup contracts 1/0, source contracts 19/0, typed scalar 1/0, generated return-route grep, and CTest registration 1/1. This closes the current typed-local script return runtime route gap; expression-direct-return scalarization outside typed-local proof scope, full typed ABI, inline structs, `in`/`out` writeback, complete 07-S5 acceptance, and stages 08-12 remain open.

Typed scalar arithmetic has a first non-helper AOT lowering slice in `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_arithmetic.c`. The function-body dispatcher routes non-const `ADD_SIGNED`, `ADD_UNSIGNED`, `SUB_SIGNED`, `SUB_UNSIGNED`, `MUL_SIGNED`, `MUL_UNSIGNED`, `DIV_SIGNED`, `DIV_UNSIGNED`, `ADD_FLOAT`, `SUB_FLOAT`, `MUL_FLOAT`, `DIV_FLOAT`, `NEG_SIGNED`, and `NEG_FLOAT` to emitter helpers instead of printing `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_*` arithmetic calls. Those emitters load the source `SZrTypeValue` slots, validate the signed/unsigned/float category selected by the opcode, and emit direct C scalar expressions such as `zr_aot_left_scalar + zr_aot_right_scalar`, `-`, `*`, `/`, and `-zr_aot_source_scalar` into `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET`. Division checks zero before the generated C division, reports `divide by zero`, and exits through `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` rather than falling through after an error.

The same lowering module now covers const-specialized signed and unsigned `+`, `-`, `*`, and `/` opcode families. It reads the right-hand operand from the function constant table, formats it as a typed C literal, checks the source slot type at runtime, and emits `zr_aot_left_scalar +|-|*|/ zr_aot_right_literal`. If the constant table entry does not match the opcode's signed/unsigned contract, the generated code raises an explicit unsupported typed arithmetic constant error instead of falling back to a VM arithmetic helper.

Signed and unsigned typed `%` now follow the same direct scalar lowering shape for both register/register and register/constant opcode families. `MOD_SIGNED`, `MOD_UNSIGNED`, `MOD_SIGNED_CONST`, and `MOD_UNSIGNED_CONST` emit `zr_aot_left_scalar % zr_aot_right_scalar` or `zr_aot_left_scalar % zr_aot_right_literal`, validate the selected signed/unsigned operand category, and report `modulo by zero` before the generated C `%` expression. The quickened adjacent signed-add plus const-modulo form `ADD_SIGNED_MOD_CONST` now emits `(zr_aot_left_scalar + zr_aot_right_scalar) % zr_aot_mod_literal`, normalizes a negative divisor, and preserves the same modulo-by-zero failure behavior. Typed `MOD_FLOAT` and numeric generic `MOD` float fallback now use direct generated-C `fmod` paths; nonnumeric/meta modulo and LLVM parity remain separate contracts.

Typed signed load-const arithmetic has been split into `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_arithmetic_load_const.c` so the main typed arithmetic lowering file remains focused. `ADD_SIGNED_LOAD_CONST`, `SUB_SIGNED_LOAD_CONST`, `MUL_SIGNED_LOAD_CONST`, `DIV_SIGNED_LOAD_CONST`, and `MOD_SIGNED_LOAD_CONST` now lower to direct generated C expressions instead of routing through arithmetic runtime helpers. The generated C materializes the right-hand constant into the requested stack slot with `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET`, reads the left scalar, emits `+`, `-`, `*`, `/`, or `%`, and reports divide-by-zero or modulo-by-zero before evaluating the C operator. The same module now also covers `ADD_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK_CONST`, `SUB_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK_CONST`, `MUL_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK_CONST`, `DIV_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK_CONST`, and `MOD_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK_CONST`: generated C materializes the left source slot into the requested staging slot with direct `SZrTypeValue` assignment, then emits the same scalar C operators and zero guards. `ADD_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK_LOAD_CONST` now materializes both the left source stack value and the right constant staging slot before emitting a direct `+` expression. `ADD_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK` and `MUL_SIGNED_LOAD_STACK` share `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_arithmetic_load_stack.c` because they consume two already-materialized stack slots; the generated C reads both slots directly, validates signed integer categories, emits `zr_aot_left_scalar + zr_aot_right_scalar` or `zr_aot_left_scalar * zr_aot_right_scalar`, preserves the add path's left-type result tag, and stores multiply as `ZR_VALUE_TYPE_INT64`. The executable-subset gate accepts these signed quickening forms so they can participate in generated AOT C modules.
