Typed integer bitwise and shift operations have their own AOT lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_bitwise.c`. `BITWISE_NOT`, `BITWISE_AND`, `BITWISE_OR`, `BITWISE_XOR`, `SHIFT_LEFT_INT`, `SHIFT_RIGHT_INT`, `BITWISE_SHIFT_LEFT`, and `BITWISE_SHIFT_RIGHT` now validate integer operands and emit C `~`, `&`, `|`, `^`, `<<`, and `>>` expressions instead of direct `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Bitwise*` / `Shift*Int` helper calls. Left shifts are generated through an unsigned intermediate before casting back to `TZrInt64`, and `BITWISE_SHIFT_RIGHT` preserves the existing logical-right-shift contract by using an unsigned left operand. Shift counts are checked as `[0, 63]` before generating the shift expression so undefined C shift counts do not become silent AOT behavior.

The same bitwise lowering module now covers the integer-primitive subset for generic `SHIFT_LEFT` and `SHIFT_RIGHT` bytecodes in generated AOT C. The function-body dispatcher routes those opcodes to direct emitters instead of printing `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ShiftLeft` or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ShiftRight`. Generated C validates both operands with `ZR_VALUE_IS_TYPE_INT`, extracts signed or unsigned integer payloads through the existing integer-like helpers, checks shift counts as `[0, 63]`, writes `ZR_VALUE_TYPE_INT64` results directly, and reports `unsupported AOT generic integer shift` for non-integer/meta/dynamic operands. Generic left shift uses the unsigned intermediate `zr_aot_left_unsigned << zr_aot_shift_count`; generic right shift uses signed `zr_aot_left_scalar >> zr_aot_shift_count`.

Typed float modulo has a focused generated-C lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_float_mod.c`. `MOD_FLOAT` now validates float-like operands with `ZR_VALUE_IS_TYPE_FLOAT`, reads `nativeDouble` payloads, checks `zr_aot_right_scalar == 0.0` before evaluating the modulo, reports `modulo by zero`, and writes the `ZR_VALUE_TYPE_DOUBLE` result with `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET(... fmod(zr_aot_left_scalar, zr_aot_right_scalar) ...)`. The function-body dispatcher routes `MOD_FLOAT` through this emitter instead of printing `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ModFloat(state, &frame, ...)`, and generated modules emit `#include <math.h>` for the direct `fmod` call. Numeric generic `MOD` now uses the same generated-C math include for its float fallback; LLVM parity remains a separate future contract.

Typed power now has a focused generated-C lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_power.c`. `POW_SIGNED` and `POW_UNSIGNED` validate signed/unsigned integer operands, guard unsupported power domains with `power domain error`, emit exponentiation-by-squaring loops with `zr_aot_power_result *= zr_aot_power_base` and `zr_aot_power_exponent >>= 1`, and write `ZR_VALUE_TYPE_INT64` or `ZR_VALUE_TYPE_UINT64` results directly. `POW_FLOAT` validates float operands, emits `pow(zr_aot_left_scalar, zr_aot_right_scalar)`, and writes `ZR_VALUE_TYPE_DOUBLE`. The function-body dispatcher routes all three typed power opcodes through direct emitters instead of printing typed power runtime helper calls.

Generic `POW` now has a separate generated-C meta-boundary lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_generic_power.c`. This opcode is not primitive numeric power in the current VM; the interpreter and previous AOT helper look for `ZR_META_POW` and otherwise write `null`. Generated AOT C now keeps only the `zr_aot_generic_power_boundary` marker and `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD(ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GenericPower(state, &frame, destinationSlot, leftSlot, rightSlot))`. `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GenericPower()` validates frame slots, runs `ZrCore_Value_GetMeta(state, leftValue, ZR_META_POW)`, resets the destination to null when no power meta function exists, and reports `unsupported AOT generic power meta dispatch` when a real meta function would require dynamic dispatch. Generated C no longer expands `SZrMeta` locals, direct source/destination stack-value locals, direct `ZrCore_Value_GetMeta(state, zr_aot_left, ZR_META_POW)`, direct `ZrCore_Value_ResetAsNull(zr_aot_destination)`, or generated debug-error templates for this opcode, and it still does not call the broader `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Pow` meta-dispatch helper. Full generated meta-call execution, source-level `**` parser support, and LLVM parity remain separate future contracts.

The typed numeric comparison families now use the same lowering module. Signed, unsigned, and float `==`, `!=`, `>`, `<`, `>=`, and `<=` opcodes validate their operand category and emit direct C comparison expressions such as `zr_aot_left_scalar == zr_aot_right_scalar` into a boolean destination. This removes the direct `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Logical*` helper path for those typed numeric comparison opcodes while leaving object/meta/dynamic equality and LLVM parity on explicit future/runtime contract paths.

Typed bool logical operations have a separate narrow lowering module in `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_logical.c`. `LOGICAL_EQUAL_BOOL` and `LOGICAL_NOT_EQUAL_BOOL` validate that both operands are bool values, normalize their stored `nativeBool` payloads, and emit `zr_aot_left_bool == zr_aot_right_bool` or `zr_aot_left_bool != zr_aot_right_bool` into a boolean destination. Statically bool unary `!` now compiles to `LOGICAL_NOT_BOOL`, which validates a bool source and emits `!zr_aot_source_bool`. The function-body dispatcher routes these typed bool opcodes through direct emitters instead of printing `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_LogicalEqualBool` / `LogicalNotEqualBool` / `LogicalNot` calls for the proven-bool cases. Focused 2026-06-22 07-S5 scalar-local validation adds a local-only fast path for the same typed bool opcodes: when scalar-local analysis proves the bool destination can skip its value slot and all bool sources have already been written to `zr_aot_bN`, generated C emits `zr_aot_bool_compare_scalar_local` / `zr_aot_bool_not_scalar_local` and writes the destination bool local directly. Unproven paths keep the older `zr_aot_bool_compare_exec` / `zr_aot_bool_not_exec` fallback, and bool-local destination recording is gated by declared bool evidence so generic conversion fallback cases do not branch on undeclared bool locals.

Typed bool control flow now has a non-truthiness lowering path. `compiler_create_jump_if_false_for_condition()` emits `JUMP_IF_BOOL_FALSE` when the condition expression is statically bool, while preserving generic `JUMP_IF` for dynamic truthiness. The interpreter validates a bool frame slot and branches on `nativeBool` directly. AOT C lowers this opcode in `backend_aot_c_lowering_control.c` by reading the bool slot instead of calling `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_IsTruthy`; when the condition slot has declared bool scalar-local coverage, it synchronizes the frame slot into `zr_aot_bN` and emits `if (!zr_aot_bN) { goto ...; }`, with `zr_aot_condition_bool` retained as the fallback predicate for unproven slots. Signed numeric compare-plus-false-branch fusion now treats `JUMP_IF_BOOL_FALSE` as the same false-branch consumer as generic `JUMP_IF`, so statically typed `>`, `>=`, and `==` conditions can still collapse into `JUMP_IF_LESS_EQUAL_SIGNED`, `JUMP_IF_GREATER_SIGNED`, `JUMP_IF_NOT_EQUAL_SIGNED`, or `JUMP_IF_NOT_EQUAL_SIGNED_CONST` instead of materializing a bool temporary. AOT C lowers those fused signed branch opcodes by reading the two signed slots or a signed constant and emitting direct C comparisons such as `zr_aot_left_scalar <= zr_aot_right_scalar` or `zr_aot_left_scalar != zr_aot_right_literal` before a generated `goto`; it no longer calls `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ShouldJumpIfGreaterSigned` for the proven signed-branch family. When both fused signed branch operands have declared `i64` scalar-local coverage, the branch helper now synchronizes the frame-slot operands directly into `zr_aot_sN` locals from `zr_aot_left->value.nativeObject.nativeInt64` / `zr_aot_right->value.nativeObject.nativeInt64` and emits the branch predicate from those locals, for example `if (zr_aot_s2 <= zr_aot_s4) {`. The focused signed const branch path follows the same left-operand rule: when `JUMP_IF_NOT_EQUAL_SIGNED_CONST` has proven `i64` scalar-local coverage for the left slot, generated C syncs that frame slot into `zr_aot_sN` and emits `if (zr_aot_sN != zr_aot_right_literal) {` instead of branching on `zr_aot_left_scalar`.

AOT C scalar-local declarations now merge source typed-local evidence and SemIR destination evidence as per-slot kind flags rather than treating the slot kind as mutually exclusive. This lets a reused slot declare multiple C mirrors, for example both `zr_aot_s17` and `zr_aot_f17`, without losing either lifetime's static type evidence. The focused M2 scalar backend uses that to write signed `i64` shift and bit-not temporary destinations directly to `sN` locals when SemIR proves the destination type, such as `zr_aot_s17 = (TZrInt64)((TZrUInt64)zr_aot_s13 << zr_aot_s1);`, `zr_aot_s18 = zr_aot_s14 >> zr_aot_s1;`, and `zr_aot_s17 = ~zr_aot_s1;`, while still mirroring the result back to the existing frame slot ABI.

Typed numeric conversions now have a first direct scalar lowering slice. Explicit `<float>` casts from statically signed integer sources compile to `TO_FLOAT_SIGNED`, explicit `<float>` casts from statically unsigned integer sources compile to `TO_FLOAT_UNSIGNED`, explicit `<int>` casts from statically float sources compile to `TO_INT_FLOAT`, explicit `<int>` casts from statically unsigned integer sources compile to `TO_INT_UNSIGNED`, explicit `<uint>` casts from statically float sources compile to `TO_UINT_FLOAT`, and explicit `<uint>` casts from statically signed integer sources compile to `TO_UINT_SIGNED`; same-type casts still collapse to the source slot and dynamic/other conversions keep the generic `TO_FLOAT` / `TO_INT` / `TO_UINT` paths. The interpreter reads the source through generated-frame slots and stores direct scalar results into `SZrTypeValue` destinations. AOT C lowers these opcodes in `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_conversion.c` with `zr_aot_convert_signed_to_float`, `zr_aot_convert_unsigned_to_float`, `zr_aot_convert_float_to_signed`, `zr_aot_convert_unsigned_to_signed`, `zr_aot_convert_float_to_unsigned`, and `zr_aot_convert_signed_to_unsigned` blocks, using `(TZrFloat64)zr_aot_source_scalar`, `(TZrInt64)zr_aot_source_scalar`, `(TZrUInt64)zr_aot_source_scalar`, and an explicit `zr_aot_unsigned_to_signed_limit` formula instead of runtime conversion helpers for these proven numeric cases.

Runtime string conversion now uses an explicit AOT runtime boundary. `TO_STRING` emits `zr_aot_value_exec_to_string` and `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD(ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ToString(state, &frame, destinationSlot, sourceSlot))`; the helper resolves source and destination slots, calls `ZrCore_Value_ConvertToString`, refreshes the active call info/frame after possible meta conversion work, re-looks up the destination, and writes string/null through the centralized runtime path. Generated C no longer expands source/destination `SZrTypeValue` lookup, direct `ZrCore_Value_ConvertToString`, frame refresh, raw-object string initialization, or destination null-reset templates for `TO_STRING`. This remains a core semantic boundary because `TO_STRING` may invoke meta conversion; LLVM remains helper-backed until LLVM parity is handled.

Object and array creation now use explicit AOT runtime boundaries. `CREATE_OBJECT` emits `zr_aot_value_exec_create_object` and `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD(ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CreateObject(state, &frame, destinationSlot))`; `CREATE_ARRAY` emits `zr_aot_value_exec_create_array` and `ZR_AOT_C_GUARD(ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CreateArray(state, &frame, destinationSlot))`. The helpers resolve the destination slot, allocate the object or array, release the previous destination value, initialize the raw-object result or null fallback, and apply the array type tag inside the centralized runtime path. Generated C no longer expands direct `ZrCore_Object_New`, `ZrCore_Object_NewCustomized`, destination `SZrTypeValue` lookup, raw-object initialization, array tag assignment, or destination null reset for these opcodes.

Closure capture access now uses explicit AOT runtime boundaries. `GET_CLOSURE` / `GETUPVAL` emit `zr_aot_value_exec_get_closure_value` and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_GetClosureValue(state, &frame, destinationSlot, closureIndex)`; `SET_CLOSURE` / `SETUPVAL` emit `zr_aot_value_exec_set_closure_value` and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetClosureValue(state, &frame, sourceSlot, closureIndex)`. The helpers resolve the active closure capture, handle native and VM closures, copy values, and apply setter barriers centrally. Generated C no longer expands current-closure stack lookup, native/VM closure decoding, capture-value read/write, direct copy, or barrier templates for these opcodes.

Reset-stack fallback opcodes now use explicit AOT runtime boundaries. `RESET_STACK_NULL` emits `zr_aot_value_exec_reset_stack_null` and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ResetStackNull(state, &frame, destinationSlot)`; `RESET_STACK_NULL2` emits `zr_aot_value_exec_reset_stack_null2` and `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ResetStackNull2(state, &frame, firstSlot, secondSlot)`. The helpers own frame-slot validation, value lookup, null reset, and failure reporting. Generated C no longer expands destination/first/second `SZrTypeValue *` locals or direct `ZrCore_Value_ResetAsNull(...)` calls for the fallback reset blocks. Scalar-local skip variants remain generated marker-only paths because they prove no `SZrTypeValue` reset is needed.

This slice deliberately leaves generic/dynamic arithmetic outside the supported primitive subsets, string concatenation, bool-as-numeric helper compatibility for generic numeric arithmetic, full generic power meta-call execution, source-level `**` parsing, dynamic/meta shift behavior outside the integer-primitive generic shift subset, bool/string/object conversions, object/meta/dynamic equality, generic equality outside the primitive subset, string/object/meta/dynamic truthiness, and logical `&&`/`||` on explicit unsupported or existing helper paths. The interpreter's historical float-fallback behavior for `ADD_INT` / `SUB_INT` is also not treated as an AOT helper escape hatch; generated C now covers the integer subset directly and fails explicitly outside that subset. The remaining dynamic paths still carry VM semantics that need separate metadata or constant-materialization contracts before they can be converted to direct C expressions without silently changing behavior.

Remaining dynamic and meta SemIR opcodes keep explicit runtime or unsupported-boundary behavior until their static metadata contracts are proven. Value-type SemIR is therefore a typed-layout contract first; the interpreter is being moved onto the same layout facts in incremental source-level slices.

## Interpreter Boundary

The active interpreter now has a first source-level local `struct` value-type execution slice for primitive POD fields:

- `ZrCore_Function_ResolvePrototypeFrameFieldLayout()` resolves a struct field name to byte offset, byte size, primitive value kind, nested type id, or embedded `SZrTypeValue` marker from compiled prototype metadata.
- `execution_inline_frame_try_get_member*()` and `execution_inline_frame_try_set_member*()` resolve known inline struct receivers through `SZrFunctionFrameSlotLayout`, then load/store the primitive field directly from the frame byte span.
- `execution_inline_frame_try_copy_stack_slot()` copies inline-struct slots by layout, and can materialize a boxed/source constructor object into an inline destination by writing primitive fields at their layout offsets.
- The interpreter dispatch checks these inline-frame helpers before falling back to object/array/string member dispatch for `GET_MEMBER`, `SET_MEMBER`, `GET_MEMBER_SLOT`, and `SET_MEMBER_SLOT`.
- Quickening preserves by-value local copy intent by forwarding `GET_STACK p -> temp; SET_STACK q <- temp` into a direct inline-struct `SET_STACK q <- p` when both slots share the same inline type layout.
- Source-level by-value struct arguments now preserve inline layout facts for the caller staging slot and the callee parameter slot. When a POD struct parameter is mutated inside the callee, field stores target the callee frame byte span and do not alias the caller's source payload.
- Runtime prototype field-layout resolution can recover the entry function's prototype metadata from the active call stack when compiled child functions no longer retain owner links after quickening/compilation cleanup.
- Source-level POD struct returns now preserve inline layout facts for the caller result slot from resolved call return types. The runtime return path copies the callee inline return payload into the caller inline target span, so mutating a returned value does not alias another inline payload.
- Inline stack slot hint floors keep struct materialization, argument, and return slots from being trimmed and reused as scalar scratch while a layout-aware expression is still active.
- Primary-expression compilation tracks and returns the actual result slot. Normalizing a call expression into a requested target slot therefore copies from the known result slot instead of assuming `stackSlotCount - 1`, which is no longer reliable once inline payload slots are preserved above scalar temporaries.
- Typed bool equality, typed bool logical-not, typed signed/float negation, `JUMP_IF`, and `JUMP_IF_BOOL_FALSE` condition dispatch now read and write through frame metadata slots instead of the old flat stack mirror. This keeps scalar bool and numeric temporaries aligned with the same generated-frame layout used by inline value payloads.
- Typed signed/unsigned-to-float, float-to-signed/unsigned, and signed/unsigned integer cross-cast opcodes read and write through the same generated-frame slot accessors, keeping explicit numeric cast temporaries aligned with the inline-frame ABI. `TO_INT_UNSIGNED` uses an explicit high-bit wrap formula so `uint` values above `INT64_MAX` do not rely on implementation-defined C signed casts.

This slice intentionally stays narrow: it covers source-level local struct construction/materialization, local by-value copy, POD struct by-value parameter isolation, POD struct by-value return isolation, and primitive field get/set. Large/non-trivial hidden returns, managed/reference fields, tail-call overlap stress, and hidden-return/AOT executable body replacement remain later milestones.

## Verification

`tests/parser/test_semir_pipeline.c` compiles a `Point` struct, copies it by value, stores into a field, and loads fields. The `.zri` output must include `FIELD_ADDR`, `STORE_VALUE`, `COPY_VALUE`, and `LOAD_VALUE`.

The same SemIR suite compiles `makePoint(seed: int): Point`, stores its returned value in an inline caller slot, and verifies the `.zri` output includes `CALL_TYPED` and `RETURN_TYPED`. This is covered by `test_struct_value_type_call_and_return_emit_semir_metadata`.

`tests/parser/test_value_type_runtime.c` executes a source-level `Point` struct fixture in the interpreter. It verifies that `var q: Point = p; q.x = 7;` mutates only the copied inline payload and that both `p` and `q` occupy separate frame byte spans with field values read through layout metadata rather than fixed offsets.

The same runtime suite also verifies by-value parameter isolation: `mutate(point: Point)` writes `point.x` inside the callee, returns the mutated callee value, and the caller's original `p.x` remains unchanged.

The runtime suite now also verifies by-value return isolation: `makePoint(seed: int): Point` returns a local inline `Point`, the caller mutates the returned value, and the returned payload remains independent of the source local and other caller inline payloads. This is covered by `test_inline_struct_return_mutation_is_by_value`.

The same test suite also checks the archived AotExecIR source contract: header/source text must expose per-slot inline frame byte layout and release the sidecar. The archive is not registered as an active CMake target in the main build, so compile verification uses a constrained object compile of `backend_aot_exec_ir.c` with the removed archived `SZrAotWriterOptions` type stubbed.

The suite also checks the archived `aot_c` source contract: `backend_aot_c_value_semir.*` must expose the value SemIR lowering entry point, consume `SZrAotExecIrFrameLayout`, recognize `FIELD_ADDR` / `LOAD_VALUE` / `STORE_VALUE` / `COPY_VALUE` / `CALL_TYPED` / `RETURN_TYPED`, resolve field layout, emit `frame.slotBase` byte expressions, expose executable inline-copy, primitive field load/store, and typed call/return helpers, and be wired from `backend_aot_c_function_body.c`. The function-body source must try `backend_aot_try_write_c_value_semir_for_exec_instruction()` before old `GET_STACK` / `SET_STACK` stack-copy lowering, before old `GET_MEMBER_SLOT` / `SET_MEMBER_SLOT` runtime helpers, and before generic direct call/return helpers.

The source-contract assertions now also lock the concrete field lowering shape and typed call/return shape: byte field address, scalar `SZrTypeValue` source/destination slot access, dense `zr_aot_dense_destination` and `zr_aot_dense_source` mirrors, `memcpy` between field bytes and primitive temporaries, `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET` for load results, typed direct-call metadata resolution, `ZrCore_Function_PreCallPreparedResolvedVmFunctionWithArgumentSource`, generated thunk invocation, `ZrCore_Function_PostCall`, typed return `state->stackTop`, `ZrCore_Function_ResolvePrototypeFrameTypeLayout`, and the `ZrCore_Function_TryCopyInlineFrameReturnValue` post-call contract. Inline struct copy is locked by `zr_aot_value_exec_inline_copy`, `ZrCore_TypeLayout_CanRawCopy`, and `zr_aot_value_exec_inline_field_copy` / `ZrCore_TypeLayout_CopyInline` for non-POD field-aware copy. The same value SemIR source-contract test now also locks embedded `SZrTypeValue` field load/store with `backend_aot_c_value_field_layout_can_value_slot_exec`, `zr_aot_value_exec_field_value_slot_load`, `zr_aot_value_exec_field_value_slot_store`, and direct `ZrCore_Value_Copy` expressions that keep byte and dense VALUE views coherent. Nested inline struct field transfer is locked by `backend_aot_c_value_field_layout_can_inline_struct_exec`, `zr_aot_value_exec_field_inline_struct_load`, `zr_aot_value_exec_field_inline_struct_store`, `const SZrTypeLayout *zr_aot_field_layout`, `ZrCore_TypeLayout_CanRawCopy(zr_aot_field_layout)`, `zr_aot_value_exec_field_inline_struct_copy`, `ZrCore_TypeLayout_CopyInline(state, ...)`, and the POD `memmove` expressions that copy between the nested field span and the inline struct slot span. Resolved fields that are still unsupported remain locked by `zr_aot_value_unsupported_field_load`, `zr_aot_value_unsupported_field_store`, `fieldLayout.isPrimitivePod`, `fieldLayout.isValueSlot`, `fieldLayout.typeLayoutId`, `ZrCore_Debug_RunError`, and `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()`.

The AOT source-contract suite now also locks generated value-frame cleanup: `backend_aot_c_frame_cleanup.*` must exist, generated C must include `zr_vm_core/function.h` and `zr_vm_core/type_layout.h`, `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` must route through `ZR_AOT_C_RETURN(...)` rather than directly returning, dispatch/default/return paths must use the shared exit, cleanup must emit `zr_aot_value_frame_drop` blocks with `ZrCore_TypeLayout_DropInline`, and typed inline return must set `zr_aot_skip_drop_slot` before `ZR_AOT_C_RETURN(1)`.

The same cleanup/failure source-contract test now also locks direct generated failure reporting. The RED check first failed on missing `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state,` in `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()`, then passed after the macro emitted the generated failure message, frame/instruction metadata, and `ZR_AOT_C_RETURN(0)`, while `backend_aot_c_function_body.c` zero-initialized `ZrAotGeneratedFrame frame = {0};`. The contract forbids `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_FailGeneratedFunction(state, &frame)` in checked generated-C emission.

The same source-contract target now also locks explicit unsupported generated-instruction boundaries. `test_aot_c_source_emits_value_frame_cleanup_exit` first failed on missing `backend_aot_write_c_unsupported_instruction(file,`, then passed after invalid branch targets, default opcode lowering paths, and fallthrough paths emitted `zr_aot_unsupported_instruction`, `unsupported AOT instruction`, `ZrCore_Debug_RunError`, and `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` instead of `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReportUnsupportedInstruction`.

The same source-contract target now also locks removal of typed function-body begin-instruction emission. The older RED/GREEN path first introduced a direct `zr_aot_begin_instruction` block to replace `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_BeginInstruction`; 07-S1 supersedes that shape for typed generated C by forbidding `backend_aot_write_c_begin_instruction(` in `backend_aot_c_function_body.c`. The focused generated-product test also rejects `zr_aot_begin_instruction`, preserving the 07 environment-isolation requirement while keeping the helper body available until the later MethodInfo/observation cleanup.

The same source-contract target now also locks direct generated pending-control lowering. The RED check first failed on missing `backend_aot_write_c_pending_control_transfer(FILE *file,`, then passed after `SET_PENDING_RETURN`, `SET_PENDING_BREAK`, and `SET_PENDING_CONTINUE` emitted direct pending-control blocks with `execution_set_pending_control`, `execution_resume_pending_via_outer_finally`, target jumps through `execution_jump_to_instruction_offset`, active-frame refresh, and generated dispatch. A production scan over `backend_aot_c*.c` found no C-backend `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetPendingReturn`, `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetPendingBreak`, or `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetPendingContinue` emission.

The separate call source-contract target locks dynamic, generic, static, and meta-call boundary lowering. `test_aot_c_source_lowers_quickened_dynamic_calls_to_direct_core_calls` first failed on missing `zr_aot_direct_dynamic_function_call`, and later failed on missing SemIR-aware dispatch when a source fixture produced a `DYN_TAIL_CALL` SemIR row on a generic call bytecode opcode. `test_aot_c_source_lowers_generic_function_calls_to_direct_core_calls` first failed while `backend_aot_write_c_direct_function_call()` still emitted `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareDirectCall`, then passed after generic direct calls reused the stack-anchor/core-call template. `test_aot_c_source_lowers_static_direct_calls_to_direct_core_calls` first failed while static direct calls still emitted `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareStaticDirectCall` / `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_FinishDirectCall`, then passed after static resolved calls emitted `zr_aot_direct_static_function_call`, `ZrCore_Closure_GetMetadataFunctionFromValue`, staged call-window setup through `ZrCore_Function_GetCallInfoFrameStorageTop`, `ZrCore_Function_PreCallPreparedResolvedVmFunctionWithArgumentSource`, generated thunk invocation, and `ZrCore_Function_PostCall`. `test_aot_c_source_makes_meta_calls_explicit_boundary` first failed while meta-call bytecodes still used the old prepared-call helper pair, then passed after those bytecodes emitted `zr_aot_unsupported_meta_call` and an explicit unsupported boundary. The contract now requires SemIR-aware dynamic routing, generic direct call lowering, static `zr_aot_direct_static_function_call` lowering, stack anchors, `ZrCore_Function_CallAndRestoreAnchor`, destination anchor restore, direct result copy, staged resolved VM pre/post-call setup with argument-source frame metadata, frame refresh, explicit meta-call unsupported-boundary markers, absence of `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Call(state, &frame...)` from dynamic call lowering, absence of `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareDirectCall` from generic direct-call lowering, absence of `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareStaticDirectCall` / `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_FinishDirectCall` from static direct-call lowering, and absence of `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_PrepareMetaCall` / `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_CallPreparedOrGeneric` from meta-call lowering. `tests/parser/test_aot_c_call_shared_library_smoke.c` compiles a generated C shared library for a source-level indirect call, verifies both static and dynamic direct-core call behavior in the generated C, executes it through the AOT runtime on Unix toolchains, separately executes a generated value-SemIR typed-call module to lock POD struct return C behavior, and separately compiles a hand-built meta-call fixture to lock the unsupported-boundary generated C surface without executing that intentional failure path.

The same suite now also locks the generated-module ABI surface: `zr_vm_common/include/zr_vm_common/zr_aot_abi.h` must exist in the real public include tree and expose the generated C descriptor/export types used by `backend_aot_c_emitter.c`. It also locks `SZrAotWriterOptions` and the AOT C/LLVM writer entrypoints in `writer.h`. Focused GCC/Clang syntax checks for `backend_aot_c_emitter.c`, frame cleanup, function body, value SemIR, and control lowering now use the normal public include paths without any local `SZrAotWriterOptions` typedef, so missing ABI or writer declarations no longer hide behind `.codex` verification fixtures.

`tests/parser/test_aot_c_source_contracts.c` now owns the archived AOT C source-contract assertions that were split out of `tests/parser/test_semir_pipeline.c`. The split keeps SemIR pipeline tests focused on compiler/runtime artifacts while giving AOT C lowering contracts their own growth boundary.

The AOT C source-contract suite now checks that typed scalar signed/unsigned/float arithmetic exposes dedicated emitter declarations, emits source-level C `+`, `-`, `*`, `/`, and unary `-zr_aot_source_scalar` expressions from `backend_aot_c_lowering_typed_arithmetic.c`, routes the corresponding non-const typed arithmetic opcodes from `backend_aot_c_function_body.c`, and no longer prints direct `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_*` arithmetic helper calls for those opcode families. It also checks signed/unsigned const arithmetic emitter declarations, constant literal formatting, `zr_aot_left_scalar +|-|*|/ zr_aot_right_literal` source expressions, function-body routing for const typed arithmetic opcodes, direct `ADD_SIGNED_MOD_CONST` lowering with `(zr_aot_left_scalar + zr_aot_right_scalar) % zr_aot_mod_literal`, and absence of direct const arithmetic helper strings for those signed/unsigned opcode families.

The source-contract suite now also locks primitive constant direct writes. `test_aot_c_source_lowers_primitive_constants_to_direct_value_writes` first failed on the missing `backend_aot_write_c_direct_primitive_constant` emitter, then passed after `GET_CONSTANT` immediate primitive constants were routed to direct null/scalar writes and `SET_CONSTANT` was routed to direct constant-table assignment. The contract requires the generated source markers `zr_aot_value_exec_primitive_constant` and `zr_aot_value_exec_set_constant`, the direct `ZR_VALUE_FAST_SET(zr_aot_destination, ...)` and `*zr_aot_constant = *zr_aot_source` shapes, and the absence of the old destination `ZrCore_Value_Copy(state, zr_aot_destination, &zr_aot_constant)` and generated-C `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetConstant(state, &frame...)` paths. The hand-written ExecBC/AOT backend fixture now verifies the same C-side direct `SET_CONSTANT` shape while preserving the current LLVM expectation that still calls `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_SetConstant`.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 signed constant first-read validation extended the typed scalar generated-product test. Signed primitive constants with i64 scalar-local coverage now emit a `zr_aot_scalar_constant_i64_local` assignment block before the current frame-write fallback, and the first i64 binary source path skips `frame.slotBase[0/1].value.type` checks when both operands are already written C locals. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. This is a partial 07-S2 step only: later primitive constant frame writes, scalar result frame writes, and other typed consumer frame checks remain open.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 signed bitwise source-local validation tightened the same typed scalar generated-product test. The old signed bitwise path for `zr_aot_s16 = zr_aot_s12 & zr_aot_s0` validated `frame.slotBase[12]` and `frame.slotBase[0]`, then reloaded both C locals from the frame before emitting the C `&` expression. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_i64_bitwise()` now checks `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_i64_written_before()` per source and skips frame validation/reload for already-written i64 locals, so the focused generated C keeps `zr_aot_s12` as the source of truth. The current proof is still block-local, so `slot 0` remains a conservative frame fallback in this fixture. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing; full 07-S2 remains open.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 signed shift source-local validation extended the same path to signed i64 shifts. The old shift lowering validated `frame.slotBase[15/16]` plus `frame.slotBase[1]`, then reloaded the left source and shift count before emitting `zr_aot_s19 = (TZrInt64)((TZrUInt64)zr_aot_s15 << zr_aot_s1)` or `zr_aot_s20 = zr_aot_s16 >> zr_aot_s1`. The signed shift emitter now applies the same per-source `i64_written_before` proof and keeps already-written left source locals in C; the shift count remains a frame fallback until cross-block source-local proofs cover `slot 1`. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 signed branch source-local validation removed another frame source dependency from typed scalar branch lowering. The first signed compare branch already emitted `if (zr_aot_s2 <= zr_aot_s4)`, but still built `SZrTypeValue` source pointers and checked `zr_aot_left->type` / `zr_aot_right->type` first. `backend_aot_write_c_direct_signed_branch()` now returns early with a pure C-local `if (zr_aot_s2 <= zr_aot_s4) { goto ...; }` block when both signed operands are proven written i64 locals. Constant signed branches and unproven cross-block cases still use the frame fallback. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 cross-block signed source-local validation widened the same proof from a block-local scan to conservative ExecIR must-write dataflow. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_i64_written_before()` now treats a C local as live at a block entry only when every reachable predecessor has written the same scalar kind, then still checks same-block prefix writes before the queried instruction. The focused typed scalar generated C no longer validates/reloads `frame.slotBase[2/3]` before the cross-block `zr_aot_s6 = zr_aot_s2 + zr_aot_s3` path, and constant signed branch lowering now emits `if (zr_aot_s2 != zr_aot_right_literal)` without a `SZrTypeValue` left source when the left slot is proven live. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. This is still partial 07-S2: destination frame writes and scalar result materialization remain.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 signed compare source-local validation applied the same per-source proof to scalar SemIR signed compare lowering. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_i64_compare()` now skips frame source checks and reloads for operands proven by `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_i64_written_before()`, so the focused generated C emits `zr_aot_b27 = (TZrBool)(zr_aot_s2 > zr_aot_s4)` without first validating and reloading `frame.slotBase[2/4]`. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. The bool destination still uses the current frame-backed result materialization, so this remains partial 07-S2.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 signed conversion source-local validation applied the same written-before proof to signed-source numeric conversions. `backend_aot_try_write_c_scalar_conversion()` now passes the current exec instruction index into conversion emitters, allowing `TO_FLOAT_SIGNED` and `TO_UINT_SIGNED` to skip `frame.slotBase[2]` source assignment, source signed-type check, and reload when `zr_aot_s2` is proven written. The focused generated C keeps the direct casts `zr_aot_f31 = (TZrFloat64)zr_aot_s2` and `zr_aot_u31 = (TZrUInt64)zr_aot_s2`. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Float-source and unsigned-source conversions still use frame-backed source reads until their written-before queries are exposed.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 unsigned source-local validation exposed the same must-write query for `u64` locals. Unsigned compare lowering, u64 bitwise binary lowering, and u64 bit-not lowering now skip source frame checks and reloads when `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_u64_written_before()` proves the source local is live. The focused generated C keeps `zr_aot_b14 = (TZrBool)(zr_aot_u8 > zr_aot_u7)`, `zr_aot_b23 = (TZrBool)(zr_aot_u21 <= zr_aot_u7)`, and `zr_aot_u33 = ~zr_aot_u7` without preceding source refreshes. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Unsigned shift, unsigned/float conversions, float sources, destination frame writes, and result materialization remain open.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 unsigned conversion source-local validation then applied that `u64` proof to numeric conversions. `TO_FLOAT_UNSIGNED` and `TO_INT_UNSIGNED` now skip `frame.slotBase[8]` source assignment, source unsigned-type check, and reload when `zr_aot_u8` is proven written, while preserving the direct `(TZrFloat64)zr_aot_u8` cast and unsigned-to-signed wrap expression. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Float-source conversion reads remain frame-backed until `f64` written-before queries are exposed.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 unsigned shift source-local validation completed the next u64 consumer slice. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_u64_shift()` now queries `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_u64_written_before()` for the left operand and `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_i64_written_before()` for the shift count, so the focused generated C keeps `zr_aot_u13 = zr_aot_u8 << zr_aot_s1` and `zr_aot_u14 = zr_aot_u10 >> zr_aot_s1` without source frame type checks or reloads when both sources are proven live. The shift-count range guard is preserved. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Float sources, destination frame writes, and result materialization remain open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 f64 source-local validation exposed the same written-before proof for float scalar locals. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_f64_binary()` now skips source frame type checks and reloads for `zr_aot_f19` / `zr_aot_f20` when both operands are proven written, while `TO_INT_FLOAT` and `TO_UINT_FLOAT` reuse proven `zr_aot_f19` directly for `zr_aot_s31 = (TZrInt64)zr_aot_f19` and `zr_aot_u31 = (TZrUInt64)zr_aot_f19`. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Destination frame writes, generic float copy/type checks, and return/result materialization remain open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 f64 stack-copy local-only validation removed the next frame-backed copy shape for float scalar locals. When both source and destination have `f64` C locals, `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_stack_copy_f64()` now emits direct assignments such as `zr_aot_f40 = zr_aot_f19;` and `zr_aot_f22 = zr_aot_f40;` instead of building `SZrTypeValue` source/destination pointers, checking source float tags, releasing destination slots, and writing `ZR_VALUE_TYPE_DOUBLE` frame payloads. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Non-f64 stack-copy frame writes, scalar result materialization, and return/result frame fallbacks remain open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 scalar stack-copy local-only validation extended the same frame-write elimination to bool, signed i64, and unsigned u64 scalar copies. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_stack_copy_bool()`, `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_stack_copy_i64()`, and `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_stack_copy_u64()` now emit direct local assignments when source and destination both have scalar locals, including `zr_aot_b5 = (TZrBool)(zr_aot_b7 != 0u);`, `zr_aot_u9 = zr_aot_u12;`, `zr_aot_u21 = zr_aot_u33;`, `zr_aot_s13 = zr_aot_s16;`, and `zr_aot_s18 = zr_aot_s19;`. Those focused copies no longer build source/destination `SZrTypeValue` pointers, perform source tag checks, release destination frame slots, or write destination frame payload fields. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Result materialization, primitive constant frame writes, and return/result frame fallbacks remain open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 unsigned compare bool result-local validation extended the result-skip proof from u64 values to bool scalar locals. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_u64_compare()` now calls `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_bool_result_can_skip_value_slot()` after proving both u64 sources are written, so the focused generated C emits only `zr_aot_b14 = (TZrBool)(zr_aot_u8 > zr_aot_u7);` and `zr_aot_b23 = (TZrBool)(zr_aot_u21 <= zr_aot_u7);` for those compare blocks. The `dstSlot=23` value is consumed directly by `JUMP_IF_BOOL_FALSE`, while the unused `dstSlot=14` value is killed by reset-stack-null; neither compare block builds `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination`, assigns `zr_aot_u_result`, or writes a bool frame payload. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar executable fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract binary passing with 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Other scalar result materialization, primitive constant frame writes, generic float copy/type checks, reset-stack-null frame writes, and boundary local restoration remain open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 i64 binary result-local validation extended the reachable result-skip proof to signed i64 scalar locals. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_i64_binary()` now calls `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_i64_result_can_skip_value_slot()` after proving signed sources are written, so the focused generated C emits only `zr_aot_s2 = zr_aot_s0 * zr_aot_s1;` for `dstSlot=2` without destination pointer, `zr_aot_s_result`, or `frame.slotBase[2]` payload write. The i64 result proof accepts signed local consumers, typed signed conversions, direct signed branches, stack-copy local consumers, and unconditional jumps while still rejecting unknown slot mentions. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract target rebuilding and executing with 19 passing tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Other scalar result materialization, primitive constant frame writes, generic float copy/type checks, reset-stack-null frame writes, and boundary local restoration remain open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 i64 bitwise result-local validation reused the same signed result-skip proof for bitwise scalar results. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_i64_bitwise()` now emits only `zr_aot_s16 = zr_aot_s12 & zr_aot_s0;` for the focused `dstSlot=16` block when both signed sources are proven written and later consumers can read the signed local. That block no longer creates a destination pointer, `zr_aot_s_result`, or a `frame.slotBase[16]` payload write. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract target rebuilding and executing with 19 passing tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Other signed bitwise results, shifts, conversions, reset-stack-null frame writes, and remaining scalar result materialization stay open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 i64 shift result-local validation reused the signed result-skip proof for shift results while preserving the semantic range guard. `backend_aot_write_c_scalar_i64_shift()` now emits only the guard and `zr_aot_s19 = (TZrInt64)((TZrUInt64)zr_aot_s15 << zr_aot_s1);` for the focused `dstSlot=19` block when both signed sources are proven written and later consumers can read the signed local. That shift block no longer creates a destination pointer, `zr_aot_s_result`, or a `frame.slotBase[19]` payload write. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract target passing 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Other signed shift results, bit-not, conversions, reset-stack-null frame writes, and remaining scalar result materialization stay open for later 07-S2 slices.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 i64 direct-return local validation removed the first return-boundary frame result fallback for scalar results. `backend_aot_write_c_direct_return_i64_local()` now emits `zr_aot_direct_return_i64_local` blocks that write the caller result value directly from `zr_aot_s23` or `zr_aot_s48` instead of constructing `zr_aot_result_slot = frame.slotBase + N` and copying through `zr_aot_result_value`. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_can_direct_return_i64_local()` centralizes the conservative gate for this path, and the i64 result-skip proof can now stop at a same-slot `FUNCTION_RETURN` when that return will consume the proven scalar local. Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 RESET_STACK_NULL scalar-local validation removed the first single-slot reset frame write from the typed scalar hot path. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_reset_can_skip_value_slot()` now proves a scalar-local reset is dead when all reachable paths overwrite or kill the slot before any source/frame read, and `backend_aot_write_c_reset_stack_null_scalar_local_skip()` emits a marker-only comment instead of the old `SZrTypeValue` destination reset block. Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 RESET_STACK_NULL2 scalar-local validation extended that reset proof to paired resets only when both slots are independently dead. `backend_aot_c_function_body.c` skips a reset2 block only if both targets pass `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_reset_can_skip_value_slot()`, and the emitter writes `zr_aot_reset_stack_null2_scalar_local_skip slots=A,B` instead of constructing two `SZrTypeValue` pointers. In that slice the first candidate `slots=3,4` was revised because the proof still treated each slot independently and did not carry paired live state; the accepted focused pair was `slots=5,6`, which is overwritten before any later read. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract target passing 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 RESET_STACK_NULL2 stateful-pair validation removed the remaining focused typed-scalar reset2 frame blocks. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_reset2_can_skip_value_slots()` now tracks first/second reset targets with a live bitmask through the current block suffix and successor graph, allowing the two slots to be overwritten at different instructions before any frame-dependent read. The proof also now asks read predicates only for opcodes that are real scalar-local consumers, so a `GET_CONSTANT` destination is treated as an overwrite rather than a read. Generated typed scalar C now contains reset2 skip markers for `slots=3,4`, `slots=5,6`, `slots=6,7`, `slots=9,10`, and `slots=15,16`, with no `zr_aot_value_exec_reset_stack_null2` block. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar fixture passing with 1 test, the source-contract target passing 19 tests, and the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passing. `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals.c` remains intentionally un-split at 2278 lines for this slice because the proof still depends on private scalar-local predicates; the smallest follow-up boundary is an extracted scalar-local liveness/result/reset proof module.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S2 i64 direct-return boundary-local validation tightened the previously accepted return-local path. `backend_aot_write_c_direct_return_i64_local()` now reuses the function-scope `zr_aot_call_info` emitted by frame setup instead of redeclaring it from `frame.callInfo` inside the return block, and no longer emits the `frame.function` null guard or constructor-name branch. The optimized route is still guarded by `backend_aot_c_scalar_locals_can_direct_return_i64_local()`, which rejects constructors before selecting this emitter. Generated typed scalar C still writes interpreter-boundary return values directly from `zr_aot_s23` and `zr_aot_s48`, preserves ownership release and closure cleanup, and no longer contains return-local `frame.callInfo`, `frame.function->functionName`, or `zr_aot_result_slot = frame.slotBase + N`. WSL GCC reports the typed scalar fixture passing with 1 test, source contracts passing 19 tests, and return contracts passing 1 test; the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passes while return-contract binaries are not registered as CTest targets in this build. `tests/parser/test_aot_c_typed_scalar.c` is now 1025 lines; this slice kept the existing focused generated-product fixture whole and records the smallest follow-up split as extracting marker/forbidden-token assertions once 07-S2 stabilizes.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S3 frame setup observation validation removed setup-time observation/default-debug initialization from `backend_aot_write_c_frame_setup()`. Focused 2026-06-21 07-S5 unsupported instruction boundary validation then routed the generated unsupported-instruction fallback through the existing `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_ReportUnsupportedInstruction()` reporter and `ZR_AOT_C_RETURN(...)` cleanup exit. Generated unsupported-instruction blocks now keep only the `zr_aot_unsupported_instruction` marker plus one cleanup-exit reporter call carrying function, instruction, and opcode indexes. The generated C no longer expands `zr_aot_instruction_index`, `zr_aot_opcode`, the hand-written `ZrCore_Debug_RunError(state, "unsupported AOT instruction")`, or a local `ZR_AOT_C_FAIL()` template in that block. WSL GCC reports the focused group passing: source contracts 19 tests, return contracts 1 test, frame setup contracts 1 test, typed scalar 1 test, value SemIR contracts 4 tests, call contracts 4 tests, call shared-library smoke 3 tests, global contracts 6 tests, and global shared-library smoke 7 tests; the unsupported-instruction shared-library smoke subtest passes, while the full shared-library smoke binary still has two unrelated execution failures in the dirty checkout. This remains an unsupported boundary, not final deopt/dynamic bridge handling.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S5 TRY boundary validation then moved generated TRY setup through `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Try()`. Generated TRY blocks now keep the existing `zr_aot_try_direct` marker plus one helper guard, while the runtime helper owns the handler push and the success-path `frame.callInfo`, `frame.slotBase`, `state->callInfoList`, and `state->stackTop.valuePointer` synchronization that was previously emitted inline. The generated C no longer expands `SZrCallInfo` recovery, `execution_push_exception_handler(state, zr_aot_call_info, ...)`, or TRY-specific generated `RunError` text in that block. WSL GCC reports source contracts passing 19 tests, control contracts 1 test, control shared-library smoke 1 test, return contracts 1 test, frame setup contracts 1 test, typed scalar 1 test, value SemIR contracts 4 tests, call contracts 4 tests, call shared-library smoke 3 tests, global contracts 6 tests, and global shared-library smoke 7 tests; the registered `aot_c_typed_scalar` CTest passes. This slice covered TRY only; END_TRY is recorded in the following focused validation note.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S5 END_TRY boundary validation then moved generated END_TRY handling through `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_EndTry()`. Generated END_TRY blocks now keep the existing `zr_aot_end_try_direct` marker plus one helper guard, while the runtime helper owns handler lookup, finally-phase mutation or handler pop, and success-path frame/call-info synchronization. The generated C no longer expands `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_destination`, `ZrCore_Value_Copy(state, zr_aot_destination, &state->currentException)`, `ZrCore_Exception_ClearCurrent(state)`, or `ZrCore_Value_ResetAsNull(zr_aot_destination)` in that block. This slice covered CATCH only; THROW is recorded in the following focused validation note.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S5 THROW boundary validation then moved generated THROW handling through `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_Throw()`. Generated THROW blocks now keep the existing `zr_aot_throw_direct` marker, reset `zr_aot_next_instruction`, call one helper guard, and dispatch only when the helper returns a non-fallthrough resume instruction. The runtime helper owns payload slot validation, pending-control cleanup, thrown-value normalization, current-frame unwind/refresh, resume-index calculation, and unhandled exception propagation through `ZrCore_Exception_Throw`. The generated C no longer expands `SZrTypeValue *zr_aot_source_value`, `SZrTypeValue zr_aot_payload`, `ZrCore_Exception_NormalizeThrownValue(state, ...)`, or THROW-specific generated diagnostics in that block. END_FINALLY is recorded in the following focused validation note.

Focused 2026-06-21 07-S5 END_FINALLY boundary validation then moved generated END_FINALLY handling through `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_EndFinally()`. Generated END_FINALLY blocks now keep the existing `zr_aot_end_finally_direct` marker, reset `zr_aot_next_instruction`, call one helper guard, and dispatch only when the helper returns a non-fallthrough resume instruction. The runtime helper owns handler pop, pending exception unwind, unhandled pending-exception propagation, pending return/break/continue resume, pending return-value copy, pending-control cleanup, frame refresh, and resume-index calculation; the unused internal `aot_runtime_resume_exception_in_current_frame()` helper was removed after the semantics moved into `ZrLibrary_AotRuntime_EndFinally()`. Generated C no longer expands the pending-control switch, `resumeCallInfo`, `handlerState`, `targetSlot`, or pending return-value copy template in that block.
